Breakage of a Pawned Coin: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on breakage of a pawned coin where weight=value=debt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on the breakage of a pawned silver coin and explain the reasoning (ta'lil) behind each.

Core Idea
Breakage of a pawn extinguishes the debt only if weight equals debt; quality loss may require a value guarantee.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq examines the specific case where a pawned silver coin has weight, value, and debt all equal (10). While complete destruction of the pawn extinguishes the debt by agreement, breakage reveals a sharp divergence among the Hanaﬁ imams. We will dissect their arguments, centering on whether the mortgagee's satisfaction (istīfā') is measured by weight or value, and how concerns about ribā and harm to the parties shape each ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base case: destruction
When the pawn is completely destroyed (hālik) while in the mortgagee's possession, all imams agree that the debt is satisfied (halaka bi-l-dayn), provided the pawn's weight and quality match the debt. This is the agreed foundation.
The agreement rests on equality in weight (wazn) and quality (jūda).
2
Note the breakage scenario and the two's options
If the coin breaks (inkasara), Abū Yūsuf and Muhammad hold that the pledgor may either take the broken piece and pay the full debt, or guarantee the full value in gold — the broken piece then becomes a new pawn for that value. This preserves the mortgagee's right to the debt without unjust enrichment.
The two argue that quality is an independent right; losing it cannot be compensated by weight alone.
3
Examine Muhammad's additional option
Muhammad adds a third option: the pledgor may let the mortgagee own the broken pawn for the debt (tamalluka bi-l-dayn). This returns to the principle that the pawn may satisfy the debt when it is of the same genus.
This option avoids ribā because the debt and the pawn are identical in type and quantity.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's core reasoning
Abū Hanīfa holds that weight (al-wazn) is the sole measure in ribawi goods. Since the pawn's weight equals the debt, its breakage does not affect the satisfaction — unless it leads to ribā or harm. In the base case (value = weight = debt), breakage still results in debt satisfaction, but if the value drops below the debt, the mortgagee must guarantee the value in gold because weight no longer covers the debt.
For Abū Hanīfa, the pledgor consented to this ruling when accepting the pawn.
5
Understand the two's objection and the tarjīḥ
The two object that breakage destroys only quality (al-jūda), not quantity. Since satisfaction (istīfā') applies to quantity, the mortgagee cannot be considered satisfied with respect to the lost quality. Imposing value is necessary to protect the pledgor from harm and avoid potential ribā. The text does not give an explicit tarjīḥ, but later Ḥanafī works tend to adopt the view of the two for breakage cases.
The thamara (practical difference) is that the pledgor has more flexibility under the two's view.

إنما يتحقق من القدر دون الجودة، ولا يمكن جعله مستوفياً باعتبار القائم لأنه لا يمكن جعل المكسور ملكاً للراهن وضمان الرهن لا يوجب الملك في العين فدعت الضرورة إلى أن يجعل مضموناً بالقيمة لأن تملك الأعيان بقيمتها مشروع وهذا تفقه وهو أن الراهن إنما رضي بقبضه بشرط ضمان الرهن فإذا تعذر إثباته لعدم رضاه بقبضه فصار كالقلب المغصوب إذا انكسر يكون مضموناً بالقيمة فكذا هذا فأما إذا كانت قيمته أقل من الوزن إن هلك يهلك بالدين عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى وعندهما يغرم قيمته من الذهب ويرجع بدينه فهما اعتبرا القيمة والجودة لا للوزن لأن في اعتبار الوزن وإسقاط الجودة اضراراً بالراهن ولا يجوز الإضرار لصاحب المال بإبطال حقه عن الجودة، وفي جعله مستوفياً لدينه بقدر قيمة القلب معنى الربا وهو استيفاء عشرة بثمانية فإذا تعذر جعله مستوفياً ضمن قيمته من خلاف وأبو حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى اعتبر الوزن والموزون في جميع الديون فصار مستوفياً لدينه بالهلاك ولا يؤدي إلى إضرار بالمرتهن بغير رضاه لأنه قبل الرهن مع علمه أن من حكم الرهن يصير مستوفياً للدين بهلاكه وصار راضياً باستيفاء جميع الدين بالهلاك متى تساويا في الوزن. وإن كان القلب أقل من قيمة دينه لأن المساواة في أموال الربا معتبرة من حيث القدر والوزن لا من حيث القيمة والجودة وإن انكسر ضمن قيمته عندهم جميعاً. أما عندهما فظاهر، وأما عند محمد فلانا لو جعلناه بالدين يؤدي إلى الإضرار وأما إذا كانت قيمته أكثر من الوزن وهلك يهلك بالدين عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى وعند محمد أيضاً لأن في الوزن والقيمة وفاء بالدين فصار بالهلاك مستوفياً لدينه وفي الزيادة أميناً. وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى : خمسة أسداس مضمونة وسدسه أمانة لأن عنده الصياغة معتبرة ومتقومة إذا لم يؤد إلى الربا فصار كأن الراهن اثنا عشر وزناً فساغ الضمان والأمانة فيهما فصير بقدر الدين مضموناً. وأما إذا انكسر ; إن انتقض بالانكسار قيمة القلب من العشرة بأن صارت تسعة أو ثمانية ضمن قيمته عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى لأن العبرة للوزن عنده وليس في الوزن من وفاء بالدين فلا يمكن إيجاب ضمان الرهن فأوجبنا القيمة. وعند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى ضمن خمسة أسداسه لأن عنده الصياغة معتبرة فتكون قيمة الرهن أكثر من الدين وذلك اثنا عشر فيكون بقدر الدين مضموناً والزيادة ،أمانة، وعند محمد رحمه رحمه الله تعالى إن شاء جعله الدين، وإن شاء افتكه بجمعية لأنه مضمون بالدين حالة الهلاك فيكون مضموناً بالدين حالة الانكسار كما بينا . وإن لم تنقض قيمة القلب من العشرة بأن كانت قيمته بعد الانكسار عشرة فالمرتهن يضمن عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى، وعند أبي يوسف رحمه الله يضمن خمسة أسداس
The first chapter: A pawn of a silver coin, its weight ten and its value ten, for ten. If it is destroyed in the possession of the mortgagee, it is destroyed for the debt by agreement, because it is equivalent in weight and quality, so satisfaction (istifa') is completed by destruction. If it breaks, then the pledgor may take the broken piece and pay off the entire debt, or he may guarantee its entire value in gold, and it becomes a pawn in its place according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, the pledgor may either own the pawn for the debt or pay the debt and take the pawn. For Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, if he takes possession of the pawn, it is not concluded as entailing its value in specie because it occurred by the owner's permission, not by transgression, so it is not a basis for guarantee of value. The contract entails satisfaction of the debt upon destruction, so the guarantee of the pawn becomes binding. When it becomes impossible to impose the value of the pawn because that would make it... he imposes the guarantee of the debt, so he makes it for the debt, unless it leads to riba or harm to one of them. Here, destruction occurred, so he made it for the debt. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), there is no way for the mortgagee to destroy the pawn for the debt because the contract is not concluded for ownership of the pawn upon destruction; it does not become owned by the mortgagee, but rather is destroyed in the ownership of the pledgor. However, the mortgagee by possession becomes satisfied with the monetary value of the item upon destruction, so the pledge's guarantee is the guarantee of satisfaction. It is not possible to consider him satisfied with respect to the lost thing by breakage, because what is lost is quality, not quantity, and satisfaction is realized from quantity, not quality. It is not possible to consider him satisfied with respect to what remains, because it is not possible to make the broken piece owned by the pledgor, and guarantee of the pawn does not necessitate ownership of the item. So necessity led to it being guaranteed by value, because owning items by their value is legislated. This is fiqh: the pledgor only agreed to possession on condition of guarantee of the pawn. When its establishment is impossible due to his lack of consent to possession, it becomes like a usurped coin: if it breaks, it is guaranteed by value. So likewise this. Now, if its value is less than its weight, if destroyed, it is destroyed for the debt according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he pays its value in gold and returns for his debt. They considered value and quality, not weight, because considering weight and dropping quality harms the pledgor, and it is not permissible to harm the owner by nullifying his right to quality. In making him satisfied with his debt to the extent of the coin's value, there is a meaning of riba: collecting ten for eight. So when it is impossible to make him satisfied, he guarantees its value in another type. Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, considered weight and the weighed in all debts, so he becomes satisfied with his debt by destruction, and it does not lead to harm to the mortgagee without his consent, because he accepted the pawn knowing that the ruling of pawn is that he becomes satisfied with the debt by its destruction when they are equal in weight. If the coin is less than the value of his debt, because equality in ribawi goods is considered in terms of quantity and weight, not value and quality. And if it breaks, he guarantees its value according to all of them. As for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is clear. As for Muhammad, because if we made it for the debt, it would lead to harm. Now if its value is greater than its weight, and it is destroyed, it is destroyed for the debt according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and also according to Muhammad, because weight and value cover the debt, so by destruction he becomes satisfied with his debt, and he is a trustee in the excess. Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, said: five-sixths are guaranteed and one-sixth is trust, because in his view craftsmanship is considered and evaluated when it does not lead to riba, so it is as if the pledgor weighs twelve, so guarantee and trust are permissible in both, and he made it guaranteed to the extent of the debt. As for breakage: if the breakage reduces the value of the coin from ten, such that it becomes nine or eight, he guarantees its value according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, because the consideration is for weight in his view, and there is not in weight coverage of the debt, so it is impossible to impose the guarantee of the pawn, so we imposed the value. According to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, he guarantees five-sixths, because in his view craftsmanship is considered, so the value of the pawn is more than the debt, that is twelve, so to the extent of the debt it is guaranteed and the excess is trust. According to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, he may either make it for the debt or redeem it in full, because it is guaranteed by the debt in the case of destruction, so it is guaranteed by the debt in the case of breakage, as we explained. If the breakage does not reduce the value of the coin from ten, i.e., its value after breakage is ten, then the mortgagee guarantees according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and according to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, he guarantees five-sixths.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage delves into the first of the three chapters identified earlier: the case where the weight of the pawned silver coin equals the debt (both 10). The author explains the rulings for two situations: destruction (هلاك) and breakage (انكسار) from the perspectives of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. In the destruction case with equal weight and value, all agree the debt is satisfied (هلك بالدين). For breakage, differences arise: the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) give the pledgor options of taking the broken piece and paying the debt or guaranteeing the value; Muhammad adds the option of owning the pawn for the debt. The reasoning revolves around whether the mortgagee's possession leads to satisfaction of the debt (استيفاء) and whether imposing the value leads to riba or harm. The text then covers subcases where value is less than weight, where Abu Hanifa holds the debt is satisfied, while the two require payment of value and return of the debt, citing harm to the pledgor and potential riba. When value exceeds weight, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say the debt is satisfied, while Abu Yusuf considers five-sixths guaranteed. For breakage with reduced value, similar divergences appear, showing how each imam applies his principle consistently.

Key Terms
الاستيفاء (al-istīfā'): The satisfaction or collection of the debt by the mortgagee through destruction of the pawn.
الهلاك (al-halāk): Complete destruction of the pawned item, extinguishing the debt or creating liability.
الانكسار (al-inkisār): Breakage of the pawned item, resulting in loss of quality but not quantity.
الجودة (al-jūda): Quality or fineness of the pawn, distinct from its weight.
الربا (al-ribā): Usury or unjust enrichment in exchange of ribawi goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abū Hanīfa, what is the ruling when a silver coin pawned for 10 (weight 10, value 10) breaks and its value drops to 8?
A) The debt is fully satisfied because weight equals debt.
B) The mortgagee must guarantee 5/6 of the value in gold; debt remains.
C) The pledgor may choose to take the broken piece or guarantee value.
D) The mortgagee owns the broken piece for the debt.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the breakage of a pawned silver coin can either satisfy the debt (by weight) or require a value guarantee (by quality), depending on which imam's principle is applied.

Destruction of a Gold Ornament Used as Collateral – Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on destruction of gold ornament collateral

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn when a gold ornament used as collateral is destroyed, and apply the principle that equality in ribawi items is by weight.

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, the collateral discharges the debt by weight, not value, because ribawi items are measured by weight.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: when a gold ornament (qalb) given as collateral is destroyed, does the debt reduce by the ornament's weight or its value? Imam Abu Hanifa insists on weight, while his two disciples consider value to avoid harming the pledgor and preventing riba. We will explore their proofs and the practical outcome of each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A gold ornament (qalb) is given as collateral (rahn) for a debt. The ornament is destroyed (halak). The question: does the debt reduce by the weight of the gold or by its market value?
The ornament has both weight and workmanship (siyagha) value.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
According to Abu Hanifa, the ornament perishes 'against the debt' (yahlak bil dayn). That means the debt is discharged to the extent of the ornament's weight of pure gold, because if the weight equals the debt's weight, the debt is fully paid; if less, proportionally.
Abu Hanifa considers only the gold content (weight), not craftsmanship.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the pledgee must pay the market value of the ornament (including craftsmanship) and then can still claim his full debt from the pledgor.
They consider value and quality, not just weight.
4
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifa: equality in ribawi items is by weight and capacity, not value. The pledgor consented to this by entering the contract. The Sahibayn: considering weight alone harms the pledgor by ignoring his property right in the workmanship, and making the pledgee a receiver of value (istifa') would constitute riba (getting more than the loan).
The Sahibayn's concern: if the ornament is worth 8 but debt is 10, the pledgee would get 10 weight of gold by value? Actually they worry about riba.
5
Determine the practical difference
In practice, if the ornament is destroyed, under Abu Hanifa the debt reduces by the weight of gold; under the Sahibayn, the pledgee must pay the value and still claim the debt. The latter prevents the pledgee from profiting from a decline in value.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether the debt is reduced or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جنسه، أنه ينعقد لتملك الرهن عند الهلاك لا يصير ملكًا للمرتهن بل يهلك على ملك الراهن ولكن المرتهن بالقبض يصير مستوفيًا لمالية العين عند الهلاك فكان ضمان الراهن ضمان الاستيفاء، ولا يمكن جعله مستوفيًا باعتبار الفائت بالانكسار لأن الفائت هو الجودة دون القدر والاستيفاء إنما يتحقق من القدر دون الجودة، ولا يمكن جعله مستوفيًا باعتبار القائم لأنه لا يمكن جعل المكسور ملكًا للراهن وضمان الرهن لا يوجب الملك في العين فدعت الضرورة إلى أن يجعل مضمونًا بالقيمة لأن تملك الأعيان بقيمتها مشروع وهذا تفقه وهو أن الراهن إنما رضي بقبضه بشرط ضمان الرهن فإذا تعذر إثباته لعدم رضاه بقبضه فصار كالقلب المغصوب إذا انكسر يكون مضمونًا بالقيمة فكذا هذا. فأما إذا كانت قيمته أقل من الوزن إن هلك يهلك بالدين عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى وعندهما يغرم قيمته من الذهب ويرجع بدينه فهما اعتبرا القيمة والجودة لا للوزن لأن في اعتبار الوزن وإسقاط الجودة إضرارًا بالراهن ولا يجوز الإضرار لصاحب المال بإبطال حقه عن الجودة، وفي جعله مستوفيًا لدينه بقدر قيمة القلب معنى الربا وهو استيفاء عشرة بثمانية فإذا تعذر جعله مستوفيًا ضمن قيمته من خلاف وأبو حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى اعتبر الوزن والموزون في جميع الديون فصار مستوفيًا لدينه بالهلاك ولا يؤدي إلى إضرار بالمرتهن بغير رضاه لأنه قبل الرهن مع علمه أن من حكم الرهن يصير مستوفيًا للدين بهلاكه وصار راضيًا باستيفاء جميع الدين بالهلاك متى تساويا في الوزن. وإن كان القلب أقل من قيمة دينه لأن المساواة في أموال الربا معتبرة من حيث القدر والوزن لا من حيث القيمة والجودة وإن انكسر ضمن قيمته عندهم جميعًا. أما عندهما فظاهر، وأما عند محمد فلانا لو جعلناه بالدين يؤدي إلى الإضرار. وأما إذا كانت قيمته أكثر من الوزن وهلك يهلك بالدين عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى وعند محمد أيضًا لأن في الوزن والقيمة وفاء بالدين فصار بالهلاك مستوفيًا لدينه وفي الزيادة أمينًا. وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى: خمسة أسداس مضمونة وسدسه أمانة لأن عنده الصياغة معتبرة ومتقومة إذا لم يؤد إلى الربا فصار كأن الراهن اثنا عشر وزنًا فساغ الضمان والأمانة فيهما فصير بقدر الدين مضمونًا. وأما إذا انكسر؛ إن انتقض بالانكسار قيمة القلب من العشرة بأن صارت تسعة أو ثمانية ضمن قيمته عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى لأن العبرة للوزن عنده وليس في الوزن من وفاء بالدين فلا يمكن إيجاب ضمان الرهن فأوجبنا القيمة. وعند أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى ضمن خمسة أسداسه لأن عنده الصياغة معتبرة فتكون قيمة الرهن أكثر من الدين وذلك اثنا عشر فيكون بقدر الدين مضمونًا والزيادة أمانة، وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى إن شاء جعله الدين، وإن شاء افتكه بجميع الدين لأنه مضمون بالدين حالة الهلاك فيكون مضمونًا بالدين حالة الانكسار كما بينا. وإن لم تنقض قيمة القلب من العشرة بأن كانت قيمته بعد الانكسار عشرة فالمرتهن يضمن عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى، وعند أبي يوسف رحمه الله يضمن خمسة أسداس القلب، وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى يضمن قدر وزنه لأن الوزن في القيمة وفاء بالدين فلم يصر مستوفيًا شيئًا من المضمون فيكون مضمونًا بالدين حالة الانكسار والوزن مضمون بالقيمة فتصير الصياغة كذلك مضمونة بالقيمة تبعًا للوزن، وعند أبي يوسف كلاهما مضمون بالقيمة أصلاً فيكون بعض الرهن مضمونًا والبعض أمانة فيشيع الضمان فيهما
Its genus: It is concluded that for possession of the collateral upon destruction, the pledgee does not become owner but it perishes as the pledgor's property, yet the pledgee by taking possession becomes a receiver of the value of the asset upon destruction. Thus the pledgor's guarantee is a guarantee of receipt. He cannot be considered a receiver with respect to what is lost by breakage because what is lost is quality not quantity, and receipt is actualized from quantity not quality. Nor can he be considered a receiver with respect to what remains because the broken piece cannot be made the pledgor's property, and guarantee of collateral does not entail ownership of the asset. So necessity compels that it be guaranteed by value because taking ownership of assets by their value is legislated. This is deduction: The pledgor agreed to its taking possession only on condition of guarantee of the collateral. When it becomes impossible to establish that due to his lack of consent to its possession, it becomes like a usurped gold ornament when broken: it is guaranteed by value. Similarly. As for when its value is less than its weight: if it perishes, it perishes against the debt according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he pays its value from gold and then claims his debt. They considered value and quality, not weight, because considering weight and omitting quality harms the pledgor, and harming the owner by annulling his right to quality is not permissible. And in making him a receiver of his debt to the extent of the ornament's value is the meaning of riba: receiving ten for eight. So when making him a receiver becomes impossible, he guarantees its value from a different type. Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, considered weight and what is weighed in all debts, so he becomes a receiver of his debt through destruction, and it does not lead to harming the pledgee without his consent because he accepted the collateral knowing that it is the ruling of collateral that he becomes a receiver of the debt through its destruction, and he became pleased with receiving all of the debt through destruction when they are equal in weight. Even if the ornament is less than the value of his debt, because equality in ribawi items is considered in terms of capacity and weight, not value and quality. And if it breaks, he guarantees its value according to all of them. As for the two, it is apparent; as for Muhammad, because if we made it against the debt it would lead to harm. And if its value is more than its weight and it perishes, it perishes against the debt according to Abu Hanifa and also according to Muhammad, because both weight and value suffice for the debt, so through destruction he becomes a receiver of his debt, and regarding the excess he is a trustee. Abu Yusuf said: five-sixths are guaranteed and one-sixth is a trust, because in his view craftsmanship is considered and has value if it does not lead to riba. So it is as if the pledgor had twelve weight, so guarantee and trust become permissible in both, and an amount equal to the debt is guaranteed. And if it breaks: if the value of the ornament from ten decreases by breakage, becoming nine or eight, he guarantees its value according to Abu Hanifa because the criterion is weight, and there is not in weight sufficiency for the debt, so guarantee of collateral cannot be imposed, so we impose value. According to Abu Yusuf, he guarantees five-sixths of it, because in his view craftsmanship is considered, so the value of the collateral is more than the debt, i.e., twelve, so an amount equal to the debt is guaranteed and the excess is a trust. According to Muhammad, if he wishes he makes it against the debt, and if he wishes he redeems it with the full debt, because it is guaranteed for the debt at the time of destruction, so it is guaranteed for the debt at the time of breakage as we explained. And if the value of the ornament from ten does not decrease, i.e., its value after breakage is ten, then the pledgee guarantees according to Abu Hanifa; according to Abu Yusuf he guarantees five-sixths of the ornament; according to Muhammad he guarantees its weight amount, because the weight in value suffices for the debt, so he did not become a receiver of any of the guaranteed part, so it is guaranteed for the debt at the time of breakage, and the weight is guaranteed by value, so the craftsmanship is also guaranteed by value, following the weight. According to Abu Yusuf, both are guaranteed by value originally, so some of the collateral is guaranteed and some is a trust, so guarantee permeates both.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a gold ornament (qalb) given as collateral (rehn). The key ruling: upon destruction (halak), the pledgee becomes a receiver of his debt to the extent of the weight of the gold, not its value, according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the pledgee must pay the value of the ornament (its price) and then still claim his debt, to avoid riba and harm. The reasoning: For Abu Hanifa, equality in ribawi items (like gold) is by weight, not value. So if the ornament's weight equals the debt's weight, destruction discharges the debt entirely. If the ornament's value is less than its weight, destruction discharges the debt only if the weight suffices? Actually the text says if value is less than weight, Abu Hanifa rules it perishes against the debt, meaning the debt is reduced by the weight of the ornament. The Sahibayn say he pays the value (market price) of the gold and then reclaims his debt. In case of breakage (inkisar), the rulings differ further. The author explains that breakage causes loss of quality (jouda) but not quantity (qadr). Since receipt of value (istifa') is only for quantity, the pledgee cannot be considered as having received anything upon breakage. Therefore, the ornament is guaranteed by its value (qima) because it becomes like a usurped item that is broken. The difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn stems from whether craftsmanship (siyagha) is considered valuable property. Abu Hanifa does not value craftsmanship; only weight matters. Abu Yusuf values it, so he apportions guarantee between the gold content and the craftsmanship. Muhammad sometimes allows the pledgee to choose to keep the broken ornament as full payment for the debt or to demand its value. The passage systematically covers scenarios of destruction and breakage when the ornament's value is less than, equal to, or more than its weight.

Key Terms
قلب (qalb): A gold or silver ornament, often used as collateral (rehn)
ضمان الرهن (daman al-rahn): The guarantee of the collateral; the obligation to compensate if the collateral is lost or damaged
استيفاء (istifa'): Receipt of value; the act of satisfying a debt by obtaining its equivalent

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when a gold ornament used as collateral is destroyed and its value is less than its weight, what happens to the debt?
A) The debt is fully discharged regardless of weight.
B) The debt is reduced by the weight of the gold in the ornament.
C) The debt remains unchanged and the pledgee must pay the market value.
D) The ornament becomes the property of the pledgee.

Key Takeaway
In a Hanafi collateral dispute, Abu Hanifa holds that debt discharge is by weight, not value, because ribawi items are measured by weight; the Sahibayn consider value to protect the pledgor's craftsmanship rights.

Breakage of a Gold Ornament Used as Collateral – The Ahkam of Inkisar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on breakage of gold ornament collateral

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the rulings for breakage of a gold ornament used as collateral across the three Hanafi imams, based on whether the breakage reduces value or not.

Core Idea
Upon breakage, loss is of quality, not quantity, so guarantee is by value, but imams differ in apportionment.

When a gold ornament used as collateral is broken (inkisar) rather than completely destroyed, the ruling changes because the loss is only in craftsmanship. This lesson explores the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on how the broken ornament is guaranteed, depending on whether the breakage reduces its market value or not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle of breakage
Breakage causes loss of quality (jouda) not quantity (qadr). Since receipt (istifa') applies only to quantity, the broken ornament cannot be considered as received. Thus necessity compels guarantee by value.
This is a general rule agreed upon.
2
Consider breakage that reduces value
If the ornament's value decreases from 10 to 9 or 8 (value < weight), Abu Hanifa rules that the pledgee guarantees the value because the weight alone does not cover the debt. Abu Yusuf guarantees five-sixths (since he values craftsmanship). Muhammad gives the pledgee an option: either take the broken ornament as full payment for the debt or redeem it by paying the full debt.
Abu Yusuf's five-sixths comes from his view that the ornament's total value is 12 (10 weight + 2 craftsmanship), and debt is 10, so 10/12 = 5/6 guaranteed.
3
Consider breakage where value does not decrease
If the value remains 10 (equal to weight), then Abu Hanifa rules the pledgee guarantees the value (since weight is not sufficient? Actually text says 'فالمرتهن يضمن' - the pledgee guarantees. But later for Muhammad: he guarantees by weight because weight suffices for debt. Abu Yusuf still five-sixths.
Muhammad's view: if weight and value both cover debt, then the pledgee is considered a receiver of debt by weight, so guarantee applies to weight, which is paid by value? Complex.
4
Synthesize the three positions
Summarize: Abu Hanifa always looks to weight; if weight is insufficient to cover debt, guarantee by value. Abu Yusuf apportions based on total value (weight + craftsmanship). Muhammad gives options or applies weight-based discharge when possible.
The differences stem from whether craftsmanship is considered valuable property.

Its genus: It is concluded that for possession of the collateral upon destruction, the pledgee does not become owner but it perishes as the pledgor's property, yet the pledgee by taking possession becomes a receiver of the value of the asset upon destruction. Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Collateral When Weight and Debt Differ
Intra-Hanafi dispute on five collateral sub-scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each of five collateral scenarios involving a gold ornament of weight 8 and debt 10, and explain the differences between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Weight governs debt discharge for Abu Hanifa; value and craftsmanship matter for the Sahibayn.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a detailed casuistic analysis of a gold ornament pawned for a debt of 10 when its weight is 8. The imams disagree on how destruction and breakage affect the debt, leading to multiple sub-rulings. Mastering this is essential for understanding Hanafi collateral law and the principles of riba avoidance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five scenarios
Recognize the five possibilities based on the ornament's value relative to its weight and the debt: equal to weight, less than weight, more than weight but less than debt, equal to debt, and more than debt.
Each scenario has a destruction and a breakage case.
2
Apply Abu Hanifa's weight-based rule
In all destruction cases, Abu Hanifa holds that the ornament is discharged by its weight (8), so the pledgee claims the remaining 2 dirhams. In breakage, the pledgee guarantees the value.
This rule avoids riba by using the standard ribawi measure (weight).
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's value-based approach
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider both value and weight, often giving the pledgee options to avoid harm. For example, when value is 9, the pledgee may choose to accept destruction by weight or pay value and claim full debt.
Craftsmanship (siyagha) is treated as having value by Abu Yusuf.
4
Examine each scenario's breakage disputes
Breakage rulings differ among the imams: sometimes the pledgee guarantees value (Abu Yusuf), sometimes the pledgor has options (Muhammad), and sometimes there is consensus.
The options aim to prevent riba and harm to either party.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is that the pledgee's recovery amount and the pledgor's rights depend on which imam's view is followed. Later fatwa often adopts the view that avoids harm.
Understanding these nuances helps in advising modern Islamic finance contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني: لو كان وزن القلب ثمانية والدين عشرة فهو على خمسة أوجه: إما إن كانت قيمته مثل وزنه أو أقل من وزنه سبعة أو أكثر من وزنه وأقل من الدين تسعة أو مثل الدين عشرة أو أكثر من الدين اثنى عشرة، وكل وجه لا يخلو إما إن هلك أو انكسر. فعند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى في فصول كلها الهلك بثمنية ويرجع على الراهن بدرهمين، والانكسار بالقيمة وفاء وفي الانكسار تعذر إيجاب ضمان الرهن ما بينا وأوجبنا ضمان القيمة. فأما عندهما إن كانت قيمته مثل وزنه يهلك بما فيه ويرجع المرتهن على الراهن بدرهمين بالإجماع، وإن انكسر ضمن قيمته عند أبي يوسف وعند محمد له خيار التمليك بالدين والإفتاك لما بينا. وإن كانت قيمته تسعة فعندهما يغرم قيمته من الذهب ويرجع بدينه لأن القيمة معتبرة عندهما مع الوزن فالوزن إن كان يفي بثمانية والقيمة لا تفي بثمانية فيخير المرتهن إن شاء رضي بهلاك الرهن بما فيه ثمانية، وإن شاء غرم قيمته تسعة ورجع عليه بدينه، وإن انكسر ضمن قيمته اتفاقًا. أما عندهما فظاهر، وأما عند محمد فلأنه لا يمكن ترك القلب عليه بثمانية من الدين لأنه إذا ترك بثمانية يتضرر به المرتهن لأن قيمة الرهن لا تفي بثمانية، وإن ترك بسبعة من جنسه يؤدي إلى الربا لأنه يصير مستوفيًا ثمانية بسبعة، وإن تعذر تركه عنده. وإن كانت قيمته أكثر من وزنه وأقل من الدين بأن كانت تسعة وهلك يهلك بوزنه عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى، وعندهما يغرم قيمته ويرجع بدينه لما بينا. وإن انكسر ضمن قيمته بالإجماع. وإن كانت قيمته أكثر من وزنه ووزنه مثل الدين بأن كانت قيمته عشرة، فإن هلك يضمن قيمته من خلاف جنسه احترازًا عن الربا والضرر، وإن انكسر فالراهن بالخيار إن شاء أفتكه بجميع الدين وإن شاء ضمنه قيمته من خلاف جنسه مثل قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله للتعذر. وعند محمد وإن كانت قيمته أكثر من وزن اثني عشر فعند أبي يوسف رحمه الله إن هلك يغرم خمسة أسداسه ويرجع بدينه لأن الصياغة عنده بمنزلة الوزن، ولو كان الوزن اثني عشر يضمن خمسة أسداسه وهو عشرة فكذا هذا. وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى إن هلك ضمن قدر الدين بخمسة أسداس القلب لأن قدر الدرهمين من قيمة الصياغة؛ أما عنده فلأنه يزيد على الوزن والدين جميعًا ولا ضمان للمالك في الأمانة. وإن انكسر انتقص بالانكسار مقدار الزيادة على العشرة فلا ضمان. وإن نقص أكثر من فضل الجودة على الدين وذلك أكثر من درهمين فالراهن بالخيار إن شاء أفتكه بجميع الدين وأخذ المكسور وإن شاء ترك عليه بقيمته مضمونًا من الذهب غير درهمين من الصياغة أربعة ووزن الرهن لا يفي بالدين فيضمن من قيمة الصياغة ما يتم به الدين وذلك درهمان فصار قدر درهمين من الصياغة
Second chapter: If the weight of the ornament is eight and the debt is ten, then it has five aspects: either its value is equal to its weight, or less than its weight like seven, or more than its weight but less than the debt like nine, or equal to the debt like ten, or more than the debt like twelve. Each aspect involves either destruction or breakage. According to Abu Hanifa, in all cases destruction is by eight and he claims two dirhams from the pledgor; breakage is by value, but in breakage it is impossible to impose guarantee of collateral as we explained, so we impose guarantee of value. According to the two (Sahibayn): if its value equals its weight, it perishes with what is in it and the pledgee claims two dirhams from the pledgor by consensus; if it breaks, he guarantees its value according to Abu Yusuf; according to Muhammad, he has the option of making it his property for the debt or redeeming it as we explained. If its value is nine, then according to the two he pays its value in gold and claims his debt because they consider value along with weight. The weight suffices for eight but the value does not suffice for eight, so the pledgee is given a choice: if he wishes, he accepts the destruction of the collateral for eight; if he wishes, he pays its value nine and claims his debt. If it breaks, he guarantees its value by agreement. As for the two, it is clear; as for Muhammad, because it is not possible to leave the ornament on him for eight of the debt, because if he leaves it for eight the pledgee is harmed since the value of the collateral does not suffice for eight; if he leaves it for seven of its type it leads to riba because he becomes a receiver of eight for seven; and it is impossible to leave it according to him. If its value is more than its weight but less than the debt, e.g., nine, and it perishes, it perishes by its weight according to Abu Hanifa; according to the two, he pays its value and claims his debt as we explained. If it breaks, he guarantees its value by consensus. If its value is more than its weight and its weight equals the debt, e.g., its value is ten, then if it perishes he guarantees its value from a different type to avoid riba and harm; if it breaks, the pledgor has the choice: if he wishes he redeems it with all the debt, if he wishes he guarantees its value from a different type, like the opinion of Abu Hanifa due to difficulty. According to Muhammad, if its value is more than weight by twelve, then according to Abu Yusuf if it perishes he pays five-sixths of it and claims his debt, because in his view craftsmanship is like weight; if the weight were twelve he would guarantee five-sixths of it, i.e., ten, so likewise here. According to Muhammad, if it perishes he guarantees the amount of the debt by five-sixths of the ornament because two dirhams are from the value of craftsmanship; according to him, because it exceeds both weight and debt, and there is no guarantee for the owner in trust. If it breaks, and the breakage reduces more than the excess over ten, then there is no guarantee. If the decrease is more than the surplus of quality over the debt, and that is more than two dirhams, then the pledgor has the choice: if he wishes he redeems it with all the debt and takes the broken piece; if he wishes he leaves it on him with its value guaranteed in gold except two dirhams from the craftsmanship of four, and the weight of the collateral does not suffice for the debt, so he guarantees from the value of craftsmanship what completes the debt, i.e., two dirhams, so two dirhams from the craftsmanship become...
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage is the second chapter (fasl) of the ruling on a gold ornament (qalb) used as collateral, specifically when the weight of the ornament is eight and the debt is ten. The author outlines five possible scenarios based on the ornament's value relative to its weight and the debt. The discussion covers both destruction (halak) and breakage (inkisar). Imam Abu Hanifa's general rule is that destruction reduces the debt by the weight of the ornament (here eight), so the pledgee claims two remaining dirhams from the pledgor. Breakage, however, requires payment of the ornament's value because the guarantee of collateral cannot apply. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider both weight and value. They give the pledgee options in certain cases to avoid riba and harm. For example, if the ornament's value is nine (more than weight but less than debt), the pledgee may choose to accept destruction for eight (the weight) or pay the value and claim the full debt. Muhammad sometimes gives the pledgor an option to redeem (iftaak) or have the pledgee guarantee the value. Abu Yusuf introduces the concept that craftsmanship (siyagha) is considered as part of the value, leading to a proportional apportionment (e.g., five-sixths guaranteed, one-sixth trust). The passage demonstrates the detailed casuistry (fiqh furu') typical of Hanafi works, applying foundational principles (like the prohibition of riba and the criteria of weight in gold) to complex real-world transactions.

Key Terms
صياغة (siyagha): The craftsmanship or labor involved in making the gold ornament, considered as having value
إفتاك (iftaak): Redemption of the collateral by the pledgor, usually by paying the full debt

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what is the ruling upon destruction of the ornament when its value equals its weight (8 dirhams) and the debt is 10 dirhams?
A) The ornament perishes by its value (8 dirhams), and the pledgee claims 2 dirhams.
B) The ornament perishes by its weight (8 dirhams), and the pledgee claims 2 dirhams by consensus.
C) The pledgee must pay the value (8 dirhams) and then claim the full debt (10 dirhams).
D) The debt is completely discharged.

Key Takeaway
For a gold ornament pawned with weight less than debt, the destruction ruling is largely agreed, but breakage triggers an intra-Hanafi dispute reflecting different prioritizations of weight, value, and harm avoidance.

Liability for Pawned Gold: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Weight vs. Value
Intra-Hanafi dispute on pawned gold liability across five value scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn) on liability for pawned gold when weight and value differ, and apply the rule to determine compensation upon destruction or breakage.

Core Idea
In pawned gold, Abu Hanifa bases liability on weight; the Sahibayn add value to prevent harm and usury.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explores a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute about a gold pawn (قلب) weighing 8 dirhams against a debt of 10 dirhams. When the pawn's value does not match its weight, differing rulings emerge upon destruction or breakage. Understanding this dispute reveals the nuanced application of qiyas and istihsan to avoid riba and harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five value scenarios
The passage lists five possibilities for the pawned object's value: equal to weight (8), less than weight (7), more than weight but less than debt (9), equal to debt (10), or more than debt (12). Each scenario has two events: destruction (هلاك) or breakage (انكسار).
The weight is fixed at 8, debt at 10.
2
Apply Abu Hanifa's rule to each scenario
Abu Hanifa holds that liability is based solely on weight. Upon destruction, the weight (8) is credited toward the debt, and the creditor claims the remaining 2 dirhams. For breakage, the entire value is due in gold to avoid usury.
Abu Hanifa views craftsmanship as subsidiary to weight.
3
Apply the Sahibayn's rule to each scenario
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider value. For value equal to weight, destruction is by consensus. For other values, they allow options: the creditor may accept the pawn at value or claim the debt. Breakage generally requires value compensation.
Muhammad sometimes gives the debtor the option to redeem or pay value.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The key difference is the amount compensated: Abu Hanifa gives a fixed credit of 8 dirhams, while the Sahibayn adjust based on actual value. This prevents the creditor from being undercompensated or the debtor from paying more than owed.
The goal is to avoid riba and harm.
5
Evaluate the underlying principles
Abu Hanifa's weight-based approach simplifies transactions and avoids valuation disputes. The Sahibayn prioritize fairness to prevent injustice. Both use istihsan to avoid usury, but differ on the measure.
The debate reflects different weights given to qiyas and istihsan.

الفصل الثاني : لو كان وزن القلب ثمانية والدين عشرة فهو على خمسة أوجه : إما إن كانت قيمته مثل وزنه أو أقل من وزنه سبعة أو أكثر من وزنه وأقل من الدين تسعة أو مثل الدين عشرة أو أكثر من الدين اثنى عشرة، وكل وجه لا يخلو إما إن هلك أو انكسر فعند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى في فصول كلها الهلاك بثمانية ويرجع على الراهن بدرهمين والانكسار بالقيمة وفاء وفي الانكسار تعذر إيجاب ضمان الرهن ما بينا وأوجبنا ضمان القيمة، فأما عندهما إن كانت قيمته مثل وزنه يهلك بما فيه ويرجع المرتهن على الراهن بدرهمين بالإجماع، وإن انكسر ضمن قيمته عند أبي يوسف وعند محمد له خيار التمليك بالدين والإفتاك لما بينا . وإن كانت قيمته تسعة فعندهما يغرم قيمته من الذهب ويرجع بدينه لأن القيمة معتبرة عندهما . مع الوزن فالوزن إن كان يفي بثمانية والقيمة لا تفي بثمانية فيخير المرتهن إن شاء رضي بهلاك الرهن بما فيه ثمانية، وإن شاء غرم قيمته تسعة ورجع عليه بدينه، وإن انكسر ضمن قيمته اتفاقاً. أما عندهما فظاهر، وأما عند محمد فلأنه لا يمكن ترك القلب عليه بثمانية من الدين لأنه إذا ترك بثمانية يتضرر به المرتهن لأن قيمة الرهن لا تفي بثمانية، وإن ترك بسبعة من جنسه يؤدي إلى الربا لأنه يصير مستوفياً ثمانية بسبعة، وإن تعذر تركه عنده . وإن كانت قيمته أكثر من وزنه وأقل من الدين بأن كانت تسعة وهلك يهلك بوزنه عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى، وعندهما يغرم قيمته ويرجع بدينه لما بينا . وإن انكسر ضمن قيمته الإجماع وإن كانت قيمته أكثر من وزنه ووزنه مثل الدين بأن كانت قيمته عشرة، فإن هلك يضمن قيمته من خلاف جنسه احترازاً عن الربا والضرر، وإن انكسر فالراهن بالخيار إن شاء أفتكه بجميع الدين وإن شاء ضمنه قيمته من خلاف جنسه مثل قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله للتعذر. وعند محمد وإن كانت قيمته أكثر من وزن اثني عشر فعند أبي يوسف رحمه الله إن هلك يغرم خمسة أسداسه ويرجع بدينه لأن الصياغة عنده بمنزله الوزن، ولو كان الوزن اثني عشر يضمن خمسة أسداسه وهو عشرة فكذا هذا. وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى إن هلك ضمن قدر الدين بخمسة أسداس القلب لأن قدر الدرهمين من قيمة الصياغة ؛ أما عنده فلأنه يزيد على الوزن والدين جميعاً ولا ضمان للمالك . في الأمانة وإن انکسر انتقص بالانكسار مقدار الزيادة على العشرة فلا ضمان. وإن نقص أكثر من فضل الجودة على الدين وذلك أكثر من در همين فالراهن بالخيار إن شاء أفتكه بجميع الدين وأخذ المكسور وإن شاء ترك عليه بقيمته مضموناً من الذهب غير در همين من الصياغة أربعة ووزن الرهن لا يفي بالدين فيضمن من قيمة الصياغة ما يتم به الدين وذلك در همان فصار قدر درهمين من الصياغة مضموناً مع الوزن وقدر در همين أمانة فيترك القلب عليه بقيمته غير در همين ولا يترك بالدين لأنه مستوفياً ثمانية بعشرة. وإن جعل مستوفياً ثمانية تضرر به الراهن يؤدي إلى الربا لأنه يصير فأوجبنا عليه القيمة من الذهب تحرزاً عن الربا ونفياً للضرر عن الرهن .
The second chapter: If the weight of the heart is eight and the debt is ten, then there are five aspects: either its value equals its weight, or less than its weight being seven, or more than its weight and less than the debt being nine, or equal to the debt being ten, or more than the debt being twelve. Each aspect is not free from either destruction or breakage. According to Abu Hanifa, in all these chapters, destruction is with eight and the creditor claims two dirhams from the debtor, and breakage is with value as fulfillment. In breakage, it became impossible to impose liability for the pawn as we stated, so we imposed liability for the value. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if its value equals its weight, it is destroyed with what is in it and the creditor claims two dirhams from the debtor by consensus. And if it breaks, he is liable for its value according to Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, he has the option of giving ownership by the debt or reclaiming (iftaak) based on what we stated. If its value is nine, according to them, he pays its value in gold and claims his debt because value is considered according to them along with weight. For weight fulfills eight and value does not fulfill eight, so the creditor may choose: if he wishes, he accepts destruction of the pawn for what is in it (eight), and if he wishes, he pays its value nine and claims his debt. And if it breaks, he is liable for its value by agreement. As for according to them, it is apparent; and as for according to Muhammad, because it is not possible to leave the heart with him for eight of the debt, because if he leaves it for eight, the creditor is harmed because the value of the pawn does not fulfill eight, and if he leaves it for seven of its kind, it leads to usury because he becomes receiving eight for seven, and leaving it became difficult for him. If its value is more than its weight and less than the debt, being nine, and it is destroyed, it is destroyed by its weight according to Abu Hanifa; according to them, he pays its value and claims his debt as we stated. If it breaks, he is liable for its value by consensus. If its value is more than its weight and its weight equals the debt, i.e., its value is ten, then if it is destroyed, he is liable for its value from a different type to avoid usury and harm. If it breaks, the debtor has the option: if he wishes, he redeems it with the entire debt, and if he wishes, he makes him liable for its value from a different type, like the statement of Abu Hanifa due to impossibility. According to Muhammad, and if its value is more than the weight of twelve, then according to Abu Yusuf, if it is destroyed, he pays five-sixths of it and claims his debt because craftsmanship according to him is like weight. If the weight were twelve, he would be liable for five-sixths of it, which is ten, so here too. According to Muhammad, if it is destroyed, he is liable for the amount of the debt with five-sixths of the heart because the amount of two dirhams is from the value of the craftsmanship. According to him, because it exceeds both weight and debt, and there is no liability for the owner over the trust. If it breaks, the decrease due to breakage is the amount of increase over ten, so no liability. If the decrease is more than the excess of quality over the debt, and that is more than two dirhams, then the debtor has the option: if he wishes, he redeems it with the entire debt and takes the broken piece; and if he wishes, he leaves it with him (creditor) for its value, liable for gold except two dirhams from the craftsmanship, which is four, and the weight of the pawn does not fulfill the debt, so he is liable from the value of the craftsmanship for what completes the debt, which is two dirhams. Thus, two dirhams of the craftsmanship become liable with the weight, and two dirhams are trust. So he leaves the heart with him for its value except two dirhams, and does not leave it for the debt because he becomes receiving eight for ten. If he makes it receiving eight, the debtor is harmed, and it leads to usury. So we imposed on him the value in gold to avoid usury and remove harm from the pawn.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute detailing rulings for a pawned gold object (قلب) with a weight of eight dirhams against a debt of ten dirhams. Five scenarios are considered based on the object's value relative to its weight and the debt: value equal to weight (8), less than weight (7), more than weight but less than debt (9), equal to debt (10), or more than debt (12). For each scenario, the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) are given for destruction (هلاك) and breakage (انكسار). Abu Hanifa consistently bases liability on weight, considering the craftsmanship (صياغة) as subsidiary. Thus, destruction results in the object's weight being applied to the debt, and the creditor recovers the balance. The Sahibayn give weight to value, allowing the creditor options and requiring compensation in gold to avoid usury. The key principle is to avoid ربا (usury) and ضرر (harm). The discussion shows the Hanafi method of qiyas and istihsan in nuanced financial transactions.

Key Terms
القلب (al-qalb): A gold object (heart-shaped or piece) used as pawn.
الصياغة (al-siyagha): The craftsmanship or workmanship value added to the metal.
الرهن (al-rahn): Pawn, pledge as security for a debt.
الضمان (al-daman): Financial liability for loss or damage.
الأمانة (al-amanah): Trust; part of the pawn that is not covered by debt.
الربا (al-riba): Usury or interest; prohibited in transactions.

Key Takeaway
Liability for pawned gold in the Hanafi school is determined either by weight (Abu Hanifa) or by value (Sahibayn), reflecting a balance between simplicity and fairness to avoid riba and harm.

Liability for Pawned Gold: Weight vs Value (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Intra‑Hanafi dispute on liability when pawn weight exceeds debt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on liability when pawn weight exceeds debt, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of their differing assumptions about craftsmanship.

Core Idea
When pawn weight exceeds debt, the liable portion is determined by weight alone (Abu Hanifa) or by value including craftsmanship (Sahibayn).

In this third chapter, the text explores five scenarios where a gold object weighing 15 dirhams is pawned for a debt of 10 dirhams, varying by its market value. The core dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples concerns whether craftsmanship (ṣiyāgha) follows weight or stands independent. This disagreement affects the proportion of liability upon destruction or breakage and the debtor's options. Let us walk through the analytical steps to unpack this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pawned object and the debt
The pawn (al-qalb) weighs 15, debt is 10. Recognise that only part of the pawn is security: 10/15 = 2/3 is liable, 1/3 is trust (amānah).
This weight‑based partition is agreed by all.
2
Understand the treatment of craftsmanship
Abu Hanifa treats craftsmanship as following the weight; it adds no independent value for liability. The Sahibayn treat craftsmanship as a separate weight or value element.
Craftsmanship is the extra value beyond raw gold weight.
3
Apply the positions to the four sub‑cases
For each scenario (value = weight, value > weight, value < weight, etc.), determine the liable portion according to each imam. Use the tables in the commentary as reference.
Focus on the two‑thirds / one‑half / or full coverage.
4
Determine the debtor's options upon breakage
When the object breaks, Abu Hanifa gives a choice: redeem (infitāk) or leave (tark) for a calculated fraction. The Sahibayn differ on whether the debtor can be compelled to redeem or has a choice based on the amount of loss.
The option of tark means the creditor keeps the object as compensation.
5
Extract the thamarah al‑khilaf
The practical difference is the proportion of liability (2/3 vs 1/2 in some cases) and whether the debtor can force redemption or choose to leave the pawn.
This directly affects the financial outcome for both parties.

Source Text

الفصل الثالث : ولو كان الدين عشرة والقلب خمسة عشر فهذا على خمسة أوجه : إما إن كانت قيمته مثل وزنه أو أكثر من وزنه أو أقل من وزنه أو أكثر من الدين أحد عشر أو مثل الدين عشرة أو أقل من الدين ثمانية وكل وجه لا يخلوا إما إن هلك أو انكسر فعند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى في الفصول كلها إن هلك يهلك بما فيه وإن انكسر فاختار الراهن الترك يترك عليه بخمسة أسداس قيمته من الذهب، وعندهما إن كانت قيمته مثل الوزن إن هلك ذهب ثلثاه بالدين والانكسار بالقيمة لأن المضمون بالرهن قدر ثلثيه وثلثة أمانة وبالإنكسار يضمن قيمة المضمون لأن عنده كان الهلاك والإنكسار بالدين لأنه أمكن جعله بالدين وتمليكه متى كان وزن ثلثيه مقيمته مثل الدين رهناً بالصياغة لم تزدد قيمته على الوزن فلا عبرة للصياغة والعبرة للوزن بعضه مضمون أمانة، فإذا نقص من قيمته بالانكسار وقع التغير بعض المضمون فيتخير وإن كان قيمته أكثر من وزنه يجوز أن تكون القيمة عشرين، فإن هلك هلك ثلثاه بالدين عندهم جميعاً لأن بثلثيه وفاء بالدين وزناً وقيمته ويهلك ثلثه أمانة، وإن انكسر ضمن ثلثيه عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى لأن المضمون من القلب عشرة والصياغة تبع للوزن فتصير الصياغة أيضاً مضمونة تبعاً للوزن ويبقى الثلث أمانة عنده، وعند أبي يوسف يضمن نصفه لأن الصياغة عنده بمنزلة الوزن وقيمتها خمسة ووزن القلب خمسة عشر فصار كان وزن القلب عشرين فيترك نصف القلب عليه بنصف قيمته، وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى ينظر؛ إن كان نقص خمسة أو أقل لم تعتبر ويجير الراهن على الانفكاك، وإن نقص أكثر من خمسة للراهن أن يسلم للمرتهن الرهن بدينه والباقي له لأن عنده القيمة زادت على الوزن فهي قيمة الصياغة وهي أمانة لأن الأمانة تصرف إلى الصياغة متى ازدادت قيمته على وزنه والفائت قدر الأمانة وبقي الدين بحالة فيجبر الراهن على الفكاك، ومتى انقضت قيمته على الوزن فقد تغير ما هو المضمون فيتخير الراهن، فإن اختار الترك يترك ثلثه بالدين ويسترد الثلث لأنه مهما تملكه بالدين لا يملك بالقيمة عنده، وإن كانت القيمة أقل من وزنه أو أكثر من الدين بأن يكون اثني عشر إن هلك يهلك ثلثاه بالدين عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى لأن بالوزن وفاء بالدين وزيادة والزيادة أمانة وعندهما يغرم عن القلب خمسة اسداسه، والأظهر أن يضمن منه قدر الدين لأن قدر الدين مضمون عليه وذلك ثلثاً القلب لأن عندهما العبرة للوزن والقيمة جميعاً وبالوزن والقيمة وفاء بالدين وزيادة والمضمون من الدين عشرة والزيادة أمانة . وإن انكسر ضمن عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله ما يساوي عشرة منه لأن عنده العبرة للوزن لا للقيمة وقدر المضمون من الوزن عشرة، وعندهما أن اختار الترك يترك عليه عشرة أجزاء من
The third chapter: If the debt is ten and the heart is fifteen, then this has five aspects: either its value equals its weight, or is more than its weight, or less than its weight, or more than the debt being eleven, or equal to the debt being ten, or less than the debt being eight. Each aspect is not free from either destruction or breakage. According to Abu Hanifa, in all these chapters, if it is destroyed, it is destroyed with what is in it; and if it breaks and the debtor chooses to leave it, it is left on him for five-sixths of its value in gold. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if its value equals its weight, if destroyed, two-thirds go for the debt, and breakage is with value because the part covered by the pawn is two-thirds, and one-third is trust. With breakage, he is liable for the value of the covered part because according to them, destruction and breakage are for the debt, since it is possible to make it for the debt and ownership when the weight of its two-thirds has a value like the debt. Pawn by craftsmanship does not increase its value over weight, so no heed is paid to craftsmanship, and heed is paid to weight. Some of it is liable, some trust. So if its value decreases by breakage, change occurs in some of what is liable, so he has a choice. If its value is more than its weight, it can be that the value is twenty. If destroyed, two-thirds are destroyed for the debt according to all of them, because with its two-thirds there is fulfillment of the debt in weight and value, and one-third is destroyed as trust. If it breaks, he is liable for two-thirds according to Abu Hanifa, because what is liable from the heart is ten, and craftsmanship follows weight, so craftsmanship also becomes liable following weight, and one-third remains trust according to him. According to Abu Yusuf, he is liable for half of it because craftsmanship according to him is like weight, and its value is five, and the weight of the heart is fifteen, so it is as if the weight of the heart is twenty. So he leaves half of the heart on him for half of its value. According to Muhammad, he looks: if the decrease is five or less, it is not considered, and the debtor is compelled to redeem (infitak). If the decrease is more than five, the debtor may submit the pawn to the creditor for his debt and retain the rest, because according to him, when value exceeds weight, it is the value of craftsmanship and it is trust, because the trust is attributed to craftsmanship whenever its value exceeds its weight, and the lost amount is the trust, and the debt remains as is. So the debtor is compelled to redeem. And when its value falls short of its weight, then what is liable has changed, so the debtor has a choice. If he chooses to leave it, he leaves one-third of it for the debt and takes back one-third, because whenever he owns it for the debt, he does not own it for value according to him. If its value is less than its weight or more than the debt, say it is twelve. If it is destroyed, two-thirds are destroyed for the debt according to Abu Hanifa, because by weight there is fulfillment of the debt and an excess, and the excess is trust. According to the two, he pays for the heart five-sixths of it. And the more apparent is that he is liable for the amount of the debt from it, because the amount of the debt is what is liable on him, and that is two-thirds of the heart, because according to them, consideration is given to both weight and value. With weight and value there is fulfillment of the debt and an excess; the liable is the debt of ten, and the excess is trust. If it breaks, according to Abu Hanifa, he is liable for the equivalent of ten from it, because according to him, consideration is given to weight not value, and the amount liable from weight is ten. According to the two, if he chooses to leave it, he leaves on him ten parts of...

Commentary
This passage is the third chapter (فصل) of the same section, discussing scenarios where the pawned gold object weighs 15 dirhams against a debt of 10 dirhams. Again, five aspects are considered based on value relative to weight and debt, ranging from value equal to weight (15), more than weight, less than weight, more than debt (11), equal to debt (10), or less than debt (8). For each, rulings on destruction and breakage are given according to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. Key concepts: the pawn is partially secured (two-thirds by weight/value) and partially trust (one-third). Abu Hanifa maintains weight as the basis, while the Sahibayn consider both weight and value, leading to options for the debtor (e.g., redeeming or leaving the object). The passage emphasizes avoiding usury and harm. The text cuts off mid-sentence, likely continuing with further details on the fifth aspect.

Key Terms
القلب (al-qalb): Gold object pawned; weight 15 in this chapter.
الثلثان (al-thuluthan): Two-thirds; proportion of pawn covered by debt according to weight.
الانفكاك (al-infitak): Redeeming the pawn by paying the debt.
الترك (al-tark): Leaving the pawn with the creditor as compensation.

Key Takeaway
When pawn weight exceeds debt, only the portion equivalent to the debt is liable; the remainder is trust, and the treatment of craftsmanship divides the Hanafi school.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Weight vs. Value in Pledging a Qalb
Intra-Hanafi dispute on weight vs. value in a pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the role of weight versus value in a pledge dispute and apply their views to scenarios of destruction and breakage.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: weight alone decides; Sahibayn: weight and value both matter.

This passage delves into a classic intra-Hanafi dispute over a pledged qalb (a coin) where the debt is 10 and the weight is 15. The core question: when the qalb is destroyed or broken, do we look solely at weight, or also at its market value? The answer affects which portion is secured and what compensation is due. We will walk through the three imams' reasoning and see how their principles play out in five key scenarios.

Guided Path
1
State the central dispute
Identify the two opposing principles: weight-only (Abu Hanifa) vs. weight-and-value (Sahibayn). Understand the role of craftsmanship (siyaghah) in this debate.
2
Map the five scenarios
The passage outlines five value-weight relationships relative to the debt of ten: value equals weight, value more than weight, value less than weight, value equals debt, value less than debt. For each, consider destruction vs. breakage.
The scenarios systematically test the principles.
3
Apply Abu Hanifa's view
For each scenario, apply his rule: the secured portion is determined by weight alone. Craftsmanship is subordinate, so value changes don't affect the weight-based fraction.
Example: if value equals weight (both 10), the entire qalb is secured, so full destruction wipes out the debt.
4
Apply the Sahibayn's views
Abu Yusuf treats craftsmanship as equal to weight, so he combines weight and value into a notional weight. Muhammad distinguishes small vs. large value differences, giving the pledgor choice in some cases.
Contrast their approaches to see the practical differences.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is clear: in breakage, the fraction of the qalb left with the creditor differs. Abu Hanifa uses weight-based fractions; Sahibayn use value-based fractions.
This affects the pledgor's compensation.

الفصل الثالث : ولو كان الدين عشرة والقلب خمسة عشر فهذا على خمسة أوجه : إما إن كانت قيمته مثل وزنه أو أكثر من وزنه أو أقل من وزنه أو أكثر من الدين أحد عشر أو مثل الدين عشرة أو أقل من الدين ثمانية وكل وجه لا يخلوا إما إن هلك أو انكسر فعند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى في الفصول كلها إن هلك يهلك بما فيه وإن انكسر فاختار الراهن الترك يترك عليه بخمسة أسداس قيمته من الذهب، وعندهما إن كانت قيمته مثل الوزن للوزن فتصير الصياغة أيضاً مضمونة تبعاً للوزن ويبقى الثلث أمانة عنده، وعند أبي يوسف يضمن نصفه لأن الصياغة عنده بمنزلة الوزن وقيمتها خمسة ووزن القلب خمسة عشر فصار كان وزن القلب عشرين فيترك نصف القلب عليه بنصف قيمته، وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى ينظر؛ إن كان نقص خمسة أو أقل لم تعتبر ويجير الراهن على الانفكاك، وإن نقص أكثر من خمسة للراهن أن يسلم للمرتهن الرهن بدينه والباقي له لأن عنده القيمة زادت على فيتخير الراهن، فإن اختار الترك يترك ثلثه بالدين ويسترد الثلث لأنه مهما تملكه بالدين لا يملك بالقيمة عنده، وإن كانت القيمة أقل من وزنه أو أكثر من الدين بأن يكون اثني عشر إن هلك يهلك ثلثاه بالدين عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى لأن بالوزن وفاء بالدين وزيادة والزيادة أمانة وعندهما يغرم عن القلب خمسة اسداسه، والأظهر أن يضمن منه قدر الدين لأن قدر الدين مضمون عليه وذلك ثلثاً القلب لأن عندهما العبرة للوزن والقيمة جميعاً وبالوزن والقيمة وفاء بالدين وزيادة والمضمون من الدين عشرة والزيادة أمانة . وإن انكسر ضمن عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله ما يساوي عشرة منه لأن عنده العبرة للوزن لا للقيمة وقدر المضمون من الوزن عشرة، وعندهما أن اختار الترك يترك عليه عشرة أجزاء من اثني عشر جزءاً من القلب باعتبار القيمة لا باعتبار الوزن لأن عندهما القيمة معتبرة مع الوزن. وإن كانت القيمة مثل الدين إن هلك يهلك بما فيه عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، وعندهما يضمن بتخيير لأن عندهما القيمة معتبرة مع الوزن ولا وفاء بالقيمة بقدر المضمون من الرهن وهي عشرة لأن قيمة العشرة من الرهن أقل من عشرة الدين فيتخير إن شاء جعله هالكاً بما فيه، وإن شاء ضمنه قيمته عشرة من الذهب فيكون رهناً عنده ويكون دينه على حالة نفياً للضرر عن نفسه. وإن انكسر ضمن مقدار ثلثي القيمة عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى لما عرف، وعندهما يضمن قيمته لأن القيمة معتبرة مع الوزن عندهما وقيمته عشرة فيترك جميع القلب عليه بعشرة. وإن كانت قيمته أقل من الدين بأن كانت ثمانية إن هلك يهلك بثلثي الدين والباقي يهلك أمانة عنده لأن عنده العبرة للوزن لا للقيمة وفي الوزن وفاء بالدين وزيادة، وعندهما يغرم قيمته ويرجع بدنه لأن عندهما القيمة معتبرة مع الوزن وفي الزيادة إن كان وفاء بالدين فلا وفاء بالقيمة وله أن يضمن قيمة القلب ثمانية فتكون رهناً عنده. وإن انكسر ضمن ثلثي قيمته عنده لما عرف وعندهما الكل لما عرف رهن عشرة دراهم بيضاً لها صرف وفضل بعشرة سود تهلك بالسود عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى. وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله : إن كانت قيمتها خمسة عشر سوداً فقد ضمن ثلثيه وثلثه أمانة كما إذا ارتهن قلباً وزنه مثل الدين وقيمته أكثر منه .
The third chapter: If the debt is ten and the qalb is fifteen, then this has five aspects: either its value is equal to its weight, or more than its weight, or less than its weight, or more than the debt (eleven), or like the debt (ten), or less than the debt (eight). Each aspect is either destroyed or broken. According to Abu Hanifa, in all chapters, if it is destroyed, it perishes with what is in it, and if it breaks and the pledgor chooses to leave it, he leaves it upon five-sixths of its value in gold. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if its value is equal to the weight, if destroyed, two-thirds go with the debt, and breakage is by value, because the portion secured by the pledge is two-thirds, and one-third is trust. With breakage, he guarantees the value of the secured portion, because according to them, destruction and breakage are by the debt, because it is possible to make it by the debt and ownership when two-thirds of its weight are equal in value to the debt. A pledge with craftsmanship does not increase its value over weight, so craftsmanship is not considered, and consideration is for weight. Part of it is secured, part trust. If its value decreases due to breakage, change occurs in part of the secured portion, so he has a choice. If its value is more than its weight—say it could be twenty—then if destroyed, two-thirds go with the debt according to all, because two-thirds suffice for the debt in weight and value, and one-third perishes as trust. If it breaks, he guarantees two-thirds according to Abu Hanifa, because the secured portion of the qalb is ten, and craftsmanship is subordinate to weight, so the craftsmanship also becomes secured subordinate to weight, and the third remains trust according to him. According to Abu Yusuf, he guarantees half, because according to him, craftsmanship is like weight, its value is five, and the weight of the qalb is fifteen, so it becomes as if the weight of the qalb is twenty; thus he leaves half the qalb upon him with half its value. According to Muhammad, he looks: if the deficiency is five or less, it is not considered, and the pledgor is forced to redeem; if the deficiency is more than five, the pledgor may hand over the pledge for his debt and keep the remainder, because according to him, the value exceeds the weight, so it is the value of craftsmanship, which is trust, because trust is allocated to craftsmanship when its value exceeds its weight, and the loss is the amount of trust, and the debt remains as is; so the pledgor is forced to redeem. And when the value equals the weight, then the secured portion has changed, so the pledgor has a choice. If he chooses to leave, he leaves one-third with the debt and takes back one-third, because when he owns it with the debt, he does not own it by value according to him. If the value is less than its weight or more than the debt, such as twelve, then if destroyed, two-thirds go with the debt according to Abu Hanifa, because by weight the debt is satisfied and there is an excess, and the excess is trust. According to the two, he pays five-sixths of the qalb, and the apparent is that he guarantees the amount of the debt from it, because the amount of the debt is secured upon him, and that is two-thirds of the qalb, because according to them, consideration is for both weight and value, and by weight and value the debt is satisfied and there is excess, the secured portion of the debt is ten, and the excess is trust. If it breaks, he guarantees what equals ten from it according to Abu Hanifa, because according to him consideration is for weight, not value, and the secured amount from weight is ten. According to the two, if he chooses to leave, he leaves upon him ten parts out of twelve parts of the qalb by consideration of value, not by weight, because according to them value is considered with weight. If the value is equal to the debt, if destroyed, it perishes with what is in it according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two, he guarantees with a choice, because according to them value is considered with weight, and there is no satisfaction of value to the extent of the secured portion of the pledge, which is ten, because the value of ten from the pledge is less than ten of the debt; so he has a choice: if he wishes, he makes it destroyed with what is in it, and if he wishes, he guarantees its value in gold, making it a pledge with him, and his debt remains as is, to remove harm from himself. If it breaks, he guarantees two-thirds of the value according to Abu Hanifa, as known. According to the two, he guarantees its value, because value is considered with weight according to them, and its value is ten; thus he leaves the entire qalb upon him for ten. If its value is less than the debt, for example eight, then if destroyed, it perishes with two-thirds of the debt, and the remainder perishes as trust according to him (Abu Hanifa), because consideration is for weight, not value, and in weight there is satisfaction of the debt and excess. According to the two, he pays its value and recovers the remainder of his debt, because according to them, value is considered with weight, and in the excess if there is satisfaction of the debt, there is no satisfaction by value; and he may guarantee the value of the qalb, eight, making it a pledge with him. If it breaks, he guarantees two-thirds of its value according to him, as known; according to the two, all, as known. A pledge of ten white dirhams having exchange and preference with ten black dirhams perishes with the black according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: if their value is fifteen black dirhams, then two-thirds are secured and one-third is trust, as when one pledges a qalb whose weight equals the debt and whose value is more than it.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal treatment of a pledged qalb (a coin or metal piece) when the debt is ten and the weight of the qalb is fifteen. The ruling depends on circumstances: whether the value equals, exceeds, or is less than weight, and whether the qalb is destroyed or broken. Abu Hanifa gives weight exclusive consideration, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider both weight and value. The practical difference appears in the amount the creditor must pay or the portion of the pledge that remains secured. The text comprehensively lays out five scenarios, each with subcases of destruction and breakage. The commentary follows the author's order, presenting each scenario with the views of the three imams. Notably, Muhammad's position often introduces a condition of the amount of deficiency or a choice for the pledgor. The final part extends the discussion to white and black dirhams, showing a similar dispute.

Key Terms
قلب (qalb): A coin or metal piece; here specifically a silver item of known weight and value.
صياغة (siyaghah): Craftsmanship or making charge; the added value due to the workmanship on the metal.
انكسار (inksar): Breaking or damage to the pledged item that reduces its value but does not destroy it entirely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 2/3
B) 5/6
C) 10/12
D) 1/2

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi pledge law, the core dispute is whether weight alone or weight combined with value determines the secured portion, with Abu Hanifa favoring weight and the Sahibayn adding value considerations.

Pledging a Ring with a Gemstone: Weight vs. Value in Hanafi Rahn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on allocation in destroyed pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on allocating debt discharge when a pledged ring with a gemstone is destroyed, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Weight governs the metal; value governs the gemstone—Abu Hanifa separates them, the Sahibayn balance both.

This lesson delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute about a silver ring set with a valuable gemstone. When such a ring is pledged and lost, how is the debt discharged? The disagreement stems from whether the 'consideration' (al-ibra) is based solely on weight (as Abu Hanifa holds) or on both weight and value (as the Sahibayn maintain). Understanding this nuance is essential for correct pledge calculations.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two cases: qalb and ring
The passage first mentions a silver qalb (coin) case, then the ring case. The qalb case sets the analogy for weight-based treatment.
The qalb case involves a pledge of a coin of known weight; it is used as a reference for the ring case.
2
Break down the ring into components
The ring consists of the metal ring (halqa) and the gemstone (fass). The metal has weight and value; the gemstone has only value.
Weight of the ring is 1 dirham; gemstone value is 9 dirhams; total debt is 10 dirhams.
3
Apply Abu Hanifa's principle: weight-only
Abu Hanifa considers the ring's weight as decisive. The gemstone's value is allocated separately to the debt, but does not affect the ring's weight.
Thus, upon destruction, 1 dirham (ring weight) and 9 dirhams (gemstone value) are discharged, totaling the full debt.
4
Apply the Sahibayn's principle: weight and value
The Sahibayn consider both weight and value. If the ring's market value equals or exceeds its weight, the ruling is the same. If the value is less, the creditor has a choice.
The choice protects the creditor from loss when the ring's value is lower than the weight-based debt offset.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, discharge is automatic; under the Sahibayn, if the ring's value is less, the creditor can either accept the ring or hold the pledgor liable for the weight-based amount.
This ikhtilaf only arises when the ring's value is less than its weight implies.
