Pledgor's Agency for Sale of Pledge
Ruling on pledgor's agency for sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the pledgor may appoint any person to sell the pledge at maturity and explain the basis of this rule.

Core Idea
The pledgor owns the property and can delegate sale absolutely, including to the mortgagee.

At the debt's maturity, the pledgor may authorize someone to sell the pledged property to recover the debt. The Hanafi school permits the pledgor to appoint the mortgagee, the trustee, or any other person, because ownership confers the right to delegate. This lesson covers the validity and limits of such agency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is tawkīl (appointing an agent) by the pledgor to sell the pledge at maturity.
The agent can be the mortgagee, the trustee, or any other person.
2
State the ruling
Such agency is valid (sahih) because the pledgor is the owner (mālik) and has the right to delegate sale of his property.
The text says 'صح لأن الراهن مالك'.
3
Note conditions
The agency is absolute (muṭlaqan) and unconditional (munajjazan). The sale is restricted to the time of debt maturity (ḥawla al-dayn).
Implicit condition: the sale must be for the purpose of repaying the debt.
4
Understand the basis
Ownership gives the pledgor full authority to sell or delegate sale; this is a fundamental principle of property rights.
No external evidence is cited; it's based on general ownership rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كان العدل رجلين والرهن مالاً يقسم فوضعاه عند أحدهما جاز ولم يضمنا لأن اجتماعهما على حفظ جميع الرهن في الأوقات كلها وهو لا يقسم متعذر فلم يبق إمكان الحفظ إلا بالتهايؤ ومطلق الأمر بالحفظ يتصرف إلى حفظ يمكن بدلالة إحالة الأمر وذلك بالتهايؤ، والثابت دلالة كالثابت نصاً فجعل الدفع إلى أحدهما بإذن المالك فلم يضمنا. وإن كان مما يقسم يضمن القابض بالإجماع ويضمن الدافع عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى خلافاً لهما على ما عرف في الوديعة. قال رحمه الله : ( ويهلك في ضمان المرتهن) لأن يده في حق المالية يد المرتهن والمالية هي المضمونة ولو دفع العدل الرهن إلى أحدهما ضمن لأنه مودع الراهن في حق العين ومودع المرتهن في حق المالية وكل منهما أجنبي عن الآخر والمودع يضمن بالدفع إلى الاجنبي وإذا ضمن العدل قيمة الرهن بالتعدي فيه إما بإتلافه أو بدفعه إلى أحدهما وأتلفه المدفوع إليه لا يقدر العدل أن يجعل القيمة رهناً في يده لأن القيمة واجبة عليه فلو جعلها رهناً في يد يصير قاضياً ومقتضياً وبيتهما تناف ولكن يأخذانها منه ويجعلانها رهناً عنده أو عند غيره فيجوز، فإن تعذر اجتماعهما يرفع أحدهما الأمر إلى القاضي ليفعل ذلك، فإن جعل القيمة رهناً برأيهما أو برأي القاضي عند العدل الأول أو عند غيره ثم قضى الراهن الدين فقد تقدم بيانه قال رحمه الله : (فإن وكل الراهن المرتهن أو العدل أو غيرهما ببيعه عند حول الدين صح لأن الراهن مالك فله أن يوكل من ماله مطلقاً ومنجزاً من الأهل ببيع
And if the trustees are two men and the pledge is property that can be divided, and they place it with one of them, it is permissible and they are not liable, because their joint custody of all the pledge at all times is difficult when it is divisible, so there is no possibility of custody except by rotation (tahayu'). According to the passage, what is the basis for the validity of the pledgor appointing an agent to sell the pledge?
A) The mortgagee has a right to sell upon default.
B) The pledge contract mandates sale at maturity.
C) The pledgor is the owner and can delegate sale.
D) The trustee is neutral and can always sell.

Key Takeaway
The pledgor's ownership gives him the right to appoint any agent to sell the pledge at maturity, including the mortgagee.

Trustee's Liability for Misdelivery of the Pawn
Rulings on trustee's liability when delivering pawn to pawner or pledgee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a trustee's liability when he delivers the pawn to the pawner or pledgee without authorization, and state the consequences for the value if it is made a new pawn.

Core Idea
A trustee who delivers the pawn without authorization is liable to compensate both the pawner and the pledgee.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq details the trustee's liability when he mishandles the pawn. It covers two key scenarios: delivery to the pledgee (treated as delivery to a stranger) and delivery to the pawner (nullifying the pledgee's right of possession). Understanding this ruling is essential for anyone involved in pawn transactions, as it clarifies the trustee's duties and the consequences of breach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The trustee delivers the pawn to the pawner or pledgee without authorization. The ruling is that he becomes liable (yadman).
2
Locate the reasoning (talil)
The passage provides two reasons: delivery to the pledgee is like delivery to a stranger (breach of trust); delivery to the pawner nullifies the pledgee's right of possession (milk al-yad) and retention (habs), which is equivalent to destroying the pawn.
This reasoning relies on the principle that the trustee is a depositary for both parties.
3
Examine the consequence after liability
If the trustee pays the value and the parties agree to make it a new pawn, whether the pawner can reclaim that value depends on the cause of liability: if liable for delivering to pawner, the value stays with the trustee; if liable for delivering to pledgee, the pawner can take it.
This distinction is based on who suffered the actual loss.
4
Analyze the trustee's recourse against the pledgee
If the trustee delivered the pawn to the pledgee as a loan or deposit, he has no recourse if the pawn perishes. But if he delivered it as a pawn (e.g., saying 'take this as your pawn'), he has recourse because the delivery was in a guaranteed capacity.
The mode of delivery determines whether the pledgee is a borrower or a pledgee with liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن وكل الراهن المرتهن أو العدل أو غيرهما ببيعه عند حول الدين صح فإن شرطت كان في يقوم مقام المرتهن في الابتداء فكذلك في البقاء. ولو دفع العدل الرهن إلى الراهن أو المرتهن يضمن لأنه متى دفع إلى المرتهن فقد دفع الأمانة بغير إذنه كما لو دفع إلى أجنبي ومتى دفع إلى الراهن فقد أبطل ملك اليد والحبس على المرتهن فإنه يثبت له ملك اليد والحبس بقبض العدل، وإبطال ملك السيد كإبطال ملك العين في ايجاب الضمان، فإن من أتلف الرهن يضمن للمرتهن كما يضمن للراهن وإن قبضا القيمة من العدل وجعلاها رهناً في يد العدل ثم قضى الراهن دين المرتهن فأراد أن يأخذ القيمة من العدل ينظر؛ إن كان العدل ضمن بدفع الرهن إلى الراهن ليس له ذلك لأنه وصل إليه حقه فتبقى القيمة للعدل، وإن كان ضمن بدفع الرهن إلى المرتهن والراهن أخذ القيمة منه لأنه لو كان الرهن قائماً بعينه في يده بعد قضاء الدين فللراهن أخذه وكذلك أخذ بدله. ثم العدل هل يرجع بالقيمة على المرتهن ينظر؛ إن دفع الرهن إليه على وجه العارية والوديعة لا يرجع بقيمة ما دفع إليه إن كان هلك الرهن في يد المرتهن إن العدل لما ملك القيمة فقد ملك الرهن بالضمان فصار معيراً ومودعاً ملكه، فإن دفع إليه رهناً بأن قال خذ هذا رهنك خذه فاحسبه يرجع العدل عليه بالقيمة لو هلك يده لأنه ملكه بأداء الضمان وقد دفع إلى المرتهن بجهة مضمونة وهي الرهن فصار كما لو دفعه إليه على سوم القرض والبيع وهذه التعريفات ذكرها الفقيه أبو جعفر الهنداوي رحمه الله تعالى. ولو كان العدل رجلين والرهن مالاً يقسم فوضعاه عند أحدهما جاز ولم يضمنا لأن اجتماعهما على حفظ جميع الرهن في الأوقات كلها وهو لا يقسم متعذر فلم يبق إمكان الحفظ إلا بالتهايؤ ومطلق الأمر بالحفظ يتصرف إلى حفظ يمكن بدلالة إحالة الأمر وذلك بالتهايؤ، والثابت دلالة كالثابت نصاً فجعل الدفع إلى أحدهما بإذن المالك فلم يضمنا. وإن كان مما يقسم يضمن القابض بالإجماع ويضمن الدافع عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى خلافاً لهما على ما عرف في الوديعة. قال رحمه الله : ( ويهلك في ضمان المرتهن) لأن يده في حق المالية يد المرتهن والمالية هي المضمونة ولو دفع العدل الرهن إلى أحدهما ضمن لأنه مودع الراهن في حق العين ومودع المرتهن في حق المالية وكل منهما أجنبي عن الآخر والمودع يضمن بالدفع إلى الاجنبي وإذا ضمن العدل قيمة الرهن بالتعدي فيه إما بإتلافه أو بدفعه إلى أحدهما وأتلفه المدفوع إليه لا يقدر العدل أن يجعل القيمة رهناً في يده لأن القيمة واجبة عليه فلو جعلها رهناً في يد يصير قاضياً ومقتضياً وبيتهما تناف ولكن يأخذانها منه ويجعلانها رهناً عنده أو عند غيره فيجوز، فإن تعذر اجتماعهما يرفع أحدهما الأمر إلى القاضي ليفعل ذلك، فإن جعل القيمة رهناً برأيهما أو برأي القاضي عند العدل الأول أو عند غيره ثم قضى الراهن الدين فقد تقدم بيانه
If the pawner authorizes the pledgee, trustee, or others to sell it when the debt matures, it is valid. If it is stipulated, it stands in place of the pledgee initially, similarly in continuance. If the trustee delivers the pawn to the pawner or pledgee, he is liable because when he delivers to the pledgee, he has delivered the trust without permission, as if he delivered to a stranger; and when he delivers to the pawner, he has nullified the right of possession and retention for the pledgee, for the right of possession and retention is established for him by the trustee's taking possession. Annulling the master's ownership is like annulling ownership of the substance in imposing liability. For whoever destroys the pawn is liable to the pledgee as he is liable to the pawner. If they both receive the value from the trustee and make it a pawn in his hand, then the pawner pays the debt and wants to take the value from the trustee, it is considered: if the trustee was liable due to delivering the pawn to the pawner, he does not have that (right), because he has received his right, so the value remains for the trustee. If he was liable due to delivering the pawn to the pledgee, the pawner takes the value from him, because if the pawn had remained in his hand after paying the debt, the pawner could take it, and similarly his substitute. Then, does the trustee have recourse against the pledgee for the value? It is considered: if he delivered the pawn to him as a loan or deposit, he does not have recourse for the value he paid if the pawn perished in the pledgee's hand, because when the trustee owned the value, he owned the pawn by liability, so he became a lender and depositor of his own property. If he delivered the pawn to him saying, 'Take this pawn, take it and count it,' the trustee has recourse against him for the value if it perishes in his hand, because he owned it by paying the liability and delivered it to the pledgee in a guaranteed manner, which is the pawn, so it is as if he delivered it to him as a loan or sale. These definitions were mentioned by Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindawi, may Allah have mercy on him. If the trustees are two men and the pawn is property that can be divided, and they place it with one of them, it is permissible and they are not liable, because their joint custody of the entire pawn at all times when it cannot be divided is impossible; no possibility of custody remains except by alternation, and the absolute command of custody refers to possible custody, indicated by the impossibility of the command, and that is by alternation. What is established by indication is like what is established by text, so the delivery to one is with the owner's permission, so they are not liable. If it is divisible, the receiver is liable by consensus, and the deliverer is liable according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, contrary to the two companions, as known in the chapter of deposits. He (the author) said: 'It perishes under the liability of the pledgee,' because his hand regarding financial right is the hand of the pledgee, and the financial aspect is what is guaranteed. If the trustee delivers the pawn to one of them, he is liable, because he is a depositary of the pawner regarding the substance and a depositary of the pledgee regarding the financial value, and each is a stranger to the other; the depositary is liable by delivery to a stranger. If the trustee becomes liable for the value of the pawn through transgression, either by destroying it or delivering it to one of them, and the recipient destroys it, the trustee cannot make the value a pawn in his hand, because the value is obligatory upon him; if he made it a pawn in his hand, he would become both the obligor and the obligee, and the two are contradictory. Rather, they take it from him and make it a pawn with him or with another, and that is permissible. If their meeting is impossible, one of them raises the matter to the judge to do that. If they make the value a pawn by their own opinion or the judge's opinion with the first trustee or another, then the pawner pays the debt, its ruling has preceded.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from al-Hidayah's commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, detailing the trustee's (عدل) liability when he mishandles the pawn. It begins with the general rule: if the pawner authorizes the pledgee or trustee to sell the pawn at maturity, it is valid; this agency is effective and remains even if the pawner revokes or dies, as will be explained later. Then it addresses the trustee's liability for delivery: if he delivers the pawn to the pledgee without the pawner's permission, he is liable because he has breached the trust; analogously, delivery to a stranger imposes liability. If he delivers to the pawner, he nullifies the pledgee's right of possession (ملك اليد) and retention (الحبس), which were established by the trustee's own custody. Nullifying a right is like destroying the property itself, so the trustee guarantees both the pawner's and pledgee's interests. The text then considers the scenario where the trustee pays the value (due to his liability) and the parties agree to make that value a new pawn. Later, when the debt is paid, whether the pawner can reclaim that value depends on how the liability arose: if the trustee was liable for delivering to the pawner, the value stays with the trustee; if liable for delivering to the pledgee, the pawner can take it. Then the trustee's right of recourse against the pledgee is examined: if he delivered the pawn as a loan or deposit, no recourse; but if he delivered it as a pawn (saying 'take this as your pawn'), he has recourse if it perishes. Next, the case of two trustees is discussed: if the pawn is indivisible (e.g., a house), they can arrange shifts and are not liable because the command to preserve implies only what is possible. But if the pawn is divisible (e.g., cash), the one who takes possession is liable by consensus, and according to Abu Hanifa the one who delivers is also liable, disagreeing with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. This is based on the rules of deposit (وديعة). Finally, it mentions that the pawn perishes under the pledgee's liability because his hand controls the financial aspect. The passage closes with the ruling on the trustee who is liable for the value: he cannot make that value a pawn himself, but the parties or the judge can arrange for it to be held by the same or another trustee.

Key Terms
عدل (adl): A trustworthy person appointed by both parties to hold the pawn; a trustee with custodial duties.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee to compensate for loss; specifically here the trustee becomes liable to pay the value of the pawn if he misdelivers or destroys it.
ملك اليد (milk al-yad): Right of possession; the pledgee has a proprietary right to hold the pawn as security.
حبس (habs): Right of retention; the pledgee's right to keep the pawn as collateral.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a trustee delivers the pawn to the pledgee without the pawner's permission, why is he liable?
A) Because he has destroyed the pawn
B) Because he has delivered the trust without permission, like delivery to a stranger
C) Because the pledgee is a stranger to the trust
D) Because the trustee loses his fee

Key Takeaway
A trustee who delivers the pawn without authorization must compensate both parties, and the subsequent rights depend on the cause of liability.

Joint Trusteeship and Liability for Divisible Property
Rulings on two trustees with divisible property and their liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on two trustees holding divisible property, identify the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the two companions, and apply the rules of custody alternation.

Core Idea
Two trustees are not liable for indivisible property if they alternate custody, but for divisible property the receiver is liable and, according to Abu Hanifa, the deliverer is also liable.

This part of the passage addresses a common scenario: what happens when two trustees are appointed and the pawn is divisible? The text distinguishes based on whether the property can be divided. Understanding this ruling requires knowledge of the rules of joint custody and the analogy with deposit (wadi'ah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage discusses two sub-cases: (a) indivisible property (e.g., a house) and (b) divisible property (e.g., cash). The ruling differs for each.
2
Analyze the indivisible case
If the property cannot be divided, the two trustees may agree on alternating custody (تهايؤ) without liability. The absolute command to preserve is interpreted as only possible custody, which is by alternation.
The default is that joint custody is impossible, so alternation is implicitly permitted.
3
Analyze the divisible case
If the property can be divided, and the trustees place it with one of them, the receiver is liable by consensus. The deliverer (the other trustee) is liable according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions), who draw analogy with deposit.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The two companions argue that in the case of deposit, if two depositaries are appointed and one gives the deposit to the other, only the receiver is liable. Abu Hanifa distinguishes based on the nature of the trust in pawn.
The passage refers to 'ما عرف في الوديعة' (as known in the chapter of deposits).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq follows Abu Hanifa's view, and this is generally relied upon in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

فقد دفع الأمانة بغير إذنه كما لو دفع إلى أجنبي ومتى دفع إلى الراهن فقد أبطل ملك اليد والحبس على المرتهن فإنه يثبت له ملك اليد والحبس بقبض العدل، وإبطال ملك السيد كإبطال ملك العين في ايجاب الضمان، فإن من أتلف الرهن يضمن للمرتهن كما يضمن للراهن وإن قبضا القيمة من العدل وجعلاها رهناً في يد العدل ثم قضى الراهن دين المرتهن فأراد أن يأخذ القيمة من العدل ينظر؛ إن كان العدل ضمن بدفع الرهن إلى الراهن ليس Key Terms
تهايؤ (taha'yu'): Alternating custody; a mutual arrangement where each trustee takes turns holding the pawn, used when simultaneous joint custody is impossible.
قابل للقسمة (qabil li al-qisma): Divisible property that can be physically or legally divided without loss of value.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when two trustees hold a divisible pawn and one delivers it to the other, what is the consensus ruling?
A) Both are liable

Key Takeaway
Two trustees of a divisible pawn: the receiver is always liable; the deliverer's liability is disputed, but the relied-upon Hanafi position holds both liable.

Agency to Sell the Pawn and Its Legal Effect
Explains validity, minor dispute, and effect of stipulation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on agency to sell a pawn when stipulated in the contract and explain its irrevocability, distinguishing it from independent agency.

Core Idea
Agency to sell the pawn, if stipulated in the pawn contract, becomes an irrevocable part of the contract surviving death and revocation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq explains the validity of appointing an agent to sell a pawned item at debt maturity. It addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a minor’s sale after maturity and then focuses on how stipulating the agency within the pawn contract transforms it into a binding, irrevocable right that survives death, revocation, and even apostasy. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rules of rahn in practice.

Guided Path
1
Establish the general validity of agency to sell
Note that the pawner, as owner, may authorize the pledgee, trustee, or any other person to sell the pawn when the debt matures. This is valid because the pawner owns the property and can delegate authority over it.
This is a baseline ruling; no special condition is required for validity.
2
Analyze the minor issue: capacity at command vs. capacity at sale
Consider the scenario: the pawner orders an intelligent minor to sell, and the minor sells after reaching maturity. According to Abu Hanifa, the sale is invalid because the original command was void due to the minor's incapacity at the time of command. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue it is valid since capacity exists at the time of sale.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is that under Abu Hanifa the pawn remains unsold and the debt continues, while under the Sahibayn the sale is valid and the debt is discharged.
3
Evaluate the binding nature when agency is stipulated in the pawn contract
If the agency is stipulated within the pawn contract itself (e.g., 'I authorize you to sell if I fail to pay'), it becomes a description (wasf) of the contract and a right of the pledgee. Consequently, the pawner cannot unilaterally revoke it, nor does it end with the deaths of the pawner or pledgee.
This is the central point: the agency is no longer independent but integrated into the rahn contract, making it irrevocable.
4
Distinguish this special agency from independent agency
The passage lists several differences: (1) the agent here can be compelled to sell if he refuses; (2) he may sell on credit even if prohibited; (3) he may convert proceeds to the debt currency; (4) he may sell a slave substitute for a crime; (5) he is not dismissed by the pledgee's revocation because the pledgee did not appoint him.
These distinctions highlight that the agency is a right of the pledgee, not a mere permission to the pawner.
5
Consider exceptions: subsequent agency and death of the trustee
If the agency is appointed after the pawn contract (not stipulated), then according to al-Karkhi, it is revocable and ends with death, just like an ordinary agency. However, a narration from Abu Yusuf holds it is still irrevocable because it attaches to the contract. Lastly, the death of the trustee voids the agency (since the pawner consented only to that person), but the pawn itself remains valid.
These exceptions refine the general rule and show the complexity of applying the concept of 'wasf' (description).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن وكل الراهن المرتهن أو العدل أو غيرهما ببيعه عند حول الدين صح لأن الراهن مالك فله أن يوكل من ماله مطلقاً ومنجزاً. ولو أمر ببيعه صغيراً يعقل فباعه بعد ما بلغ لا يصح عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى. وقالا : يصح لقدرته عليه يقول إن أمره يقع باطلاً لعدم القدرة وقت الأمر فلا ينقلب جائزاً. قال رحمه الله : (فإن شرطت في عقد الرهن لم ينعزل بعزله وبموت الراهن والمرتهن لأن الوكالة لما شرطت في عقد الرهن صارت وصفاً من أوصافه وحقاً من حقوقه ألا ترى أنها الزيادة الوثيقة فلزم بلزوم أصله ولا يتعلق به حق المرتهن وفي العزل إبطال حقه وصار كالوكالة بالخصومة بطلب المدعي، ولو وكله بالبيع مطلقاً حتى ملك البيع بالنقد والنسيئة ثم نهاه عن البيع بالنسيئة لم يعمل نهيه لأنه لازم بأصله فكذا بوصفه وكذا لا ينعزل بالعزل الحكمي لموت الموكل وارتداده ولحوقه بدار الحرب لأن الرهن لا يبطل بموته، ولو بطل إنما يبطل لحق الورثة وحق المرتهن مقدم عليه كما يقدم على حق الراهن بخلاف الوكالة المفردة حيث تبطل بالموت وينعزل بعزل الوكيل لما عرف في موضعه، وهذه الوكالة بخلاف المفردة من وجوه منها ما ذكرنا، ومنها أن الوكيل هنا إذا امتنع عن البيع يجبر عليه بخلاف الوكالة المفردة، ومنها أن هذا الولد والأرش بخلاف المفردة ومنها أنه إذا باع بخلاف جنس الدين له أن يبيع يصرفه إلى جنس الدين بخلاف المفردة ومنها أن الرهن إذا كان عبداً وقتله عبد فدفع القاتل بالجناية كان لهذا الوكيل أن يبيعه بخلاف المفردة، وإنما لم ينعزل بعزل المرتهن لأنه لم يوكله فكان أجنبياً عنه بالنسبة إلى الوكالة وهذا إذا عزله الموكل لا ينعزل فبعزل غيره أولى أن لا ينعزل. وقيد المؤلف بقوله : شرطت في عقد الرهن فلو كانت بعد عقد الرهن ذكر الكرخي في مختصره للراهن أن يعزله وينعزل بموته لأن التوكيل بالبيع وقع منفرداً عن الرهن. وإنما جعلناها من توابع الرهن لكونها مشروطة فيه، فإذا لم تشترط في الرهن اعتبرت وكالة مبتدأة، وروي عن أبي يوسف أنه لا ينعزل وهو اختيار بعض مشايخنا لأن المشروط بعد الرهن التحق بالعقد لأن اشتراط البيع حتى يوفي دينه من ثمنه زيادة إيفاء وتأكيد شرط في الرهن لأنه يثبت في الرهن إيفاء حكمي وباشتراط البيع فيه ثبت أيضاً حقيقي وكان اشتراط زيادة أيضاً، والزيادة في المعقود عليه تلتحق بأصل العقد وصار كالمشروط فيه ابتداء وكالزيادة في الثمن. ولو مات العدل بطلت الوكالة حتى لو أوصى ببيعه لم يجز والرهن على حاله لأن الراهن رضي ببيعه ولم يرض ببيع غيره وقد وقع العجز عن البيع بنفسه ونائبه فبطلت الوكالة ضرورة، والرهن لا يبطل لأن العدل نائب عن الراهن والمرتهن في الإمساك والحفظ والرهن لا يبطل بموتهما فيموت نائبهما أولى. ولو اجتمع الراهن والمرتهن على وضعه على يدي عدل
If the pawner authorizes the pledgee, trustee, or others to sell it when the debt matures, it is valid, because the pawner is the owner, so he may authorize anyone regarding his property absolutely and unconditionally. If he orders an intelligent minor to sell it and he sells it after reaching maturity, it is not valid according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. The two (companions) say: it is valid, because he is capable. He (Abu Hanifa) says: his order is void due to incapacity at the time of the order, so it does not become valid later. He (the author) said: 'If it is stipulated in the pawn contract, it is not revoked by his revocation nor by the deaths of the pawner and pledgee, because when the agency is stipulated in the pawn contract, it becomes a description of its descriptions and a right of its rights. Do you not see that it is an increase in security, so it binds by the binding of its origin, and it is not subject to the right of the pledgee. In revocation, there is annulment of his right, and it becomes like the agency for litigation at the request of the plaintiff. If he authorized him absolutely to sell, such that he had authority to sell for cash or credit, then forbade him from selling on credit, his prohibition is ineffective, because the agency is binding in its origin, similarly in its description. Likewise, he is not dismissed by the constructive revocation of the death of the principal, his apostasy, or his joining the abode of war, because the pawn does not become void by his death. If it were to become void, it would be for the right of the heirs, but the right of the pledgee takes precedence over it, just as it takes precedence over the right of the pawner, unlike an independent agency which becomes void by death and the agent is dismissed by the principal's revocation. This agency differs from an independent agency in several ways: from what we mentioned, and that the agent here, if he refrains from selling, is compelled to do so, unlike an independent agency; and that this [includes] children and compensation, unlike an independent agency; and that if he sells for a different type than the debt, he may sell and convert it to the type of debt, unlike an independent agency; and that if the pawn is a slave and is killed by a slave, and the killer is handed over for the crime, this agent may sell him, unlike an independent agency. He is not dismissed by the pledgee's revocation because he did not appoint him, so he is a stranger regarding the agency. If the principal revokes, he is not dismissed, so it is even more appropriate that he is not dismissed by another's revocation. The author restricted by his saying: 'stipulated in the pawn contract'; if it is after the pawn contract, al-Karkhi mentioned in his Mukhtasar that the pawner may revoke him and he is dismissed by his death, because the agency for sale occurred independently of the pawn. We have made it a consequence of the pawn only when it is stipulated in it. If it is not stipulated in the pawn, it is considered a new agency. It is reported from Abu Yusuf that he is not dismissed, and it is the choice of some of our scholars, because what is stipulated after the pawn attaches to the contract, because stipulating the sale to pay his debt from its price is an increase in fulfillment and confirmation stipulated in the pawn, because it establishes in the pawn a legal fulfillment, and by stipulating the sale in it, an actual fulfillment is also established, and that is an additional stipulation. The increase in the subject matter attaches to the original contract and becomes like its initial stipulation, like an increase in the price. If the trustee dies, the agency becomes void, such that if he bequeaths its sale, it is not permissible, and the pawn remains as it is, because the pawner consented to his sale and did not consent to the sale of another; incapacity to sell by himself and his deputy has occurred, so the agency becomes void by necessity. The pawn does not become void because the trustee is the deputy of the pawner and pledgee in holding and preservation, and the pawn does not become void by their deaths, so the death of their deputy is even more appropriate. If the pawner and pledgee agree to place it with a trustee...
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion from the previous section, focusing on the agency (وكالة) to sell the pawn when the debt matures. It begins by stating the validity of such an appointment, as the pawner is the owner and can authorize anyone to sell his property. Then it discusses a case: if the pawner orders an intelligent minor to sell, and the minor sells after reaching maturity, Abu Hanifa says the sale is invalid because the order was given when the minor was incapable; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is valid because capacity is realized at the time of sale. The author (al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah) then explains that if the agency is stipulated in the pawn contract itself, it becomes an integral part of the contract (وصف من أوصافه وحق من حقوقه). Therefore, it is not revoked by the pawner's unilateral revocation, nor by the deaths of the pawner or pledgee. This is unlike an independent agency (وكالة مفردة) which ends with death or revocation. Several distinctions are listed: the agent here can be compelled to sell, can sell for credit even if forbidden, can sell for a different currency and convert to the debt currency, and can sell a slave who is the substitute for a crime. The author then addresses a restriction: if the agency is stipulated after the contract (i.e., not within the pawn contract), then according to al-Karkhi, the pawner can revoke it and it ends with death, because it is an independent agency. However, a narration from Abu Yusuf holds that even such subsequent agency is not revocable, because it attaches to the original contract. The passage ends by discussing the death of the trustee: the agency to sell is void because the pawner only consented to that specific person, but the pawn itself remains valid because the trustee is merely a deputy for custody, and the pawn survives the deaths of the principals.

Key Terms
وكالة (wakalah): Agency; the delegation of authority to another person to perform a legal act. Here specifically the authority to sell the pawn.
عزل (azl): Revocation or dismissal of the agent by the principal.
وصف (wisf): Description or attribute; the agency becomes a description of the pawn contract, meaning it is integral to it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The agency is revoked immediately
B) The agency is not revoked because it is part of the contract
C) The agency is revoked only if the pledgee agrees
D) The agency becomes void after sixty days

Key Takeaway
Stipulating the agency to sell in the pawn contract makes it a binding right of the pledgee, irrevocable and surviving death or revocation.

Agent's Binding Agency in a Pledge Contract
Ruling with proof on agency in pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why an agency conditioned in a pledge is binding and not revocable, and distinguish it from a separate agency.

Core Idea
An agency conditioned in a pledge contract becomes a binding part of the contract, not revocable like a separate agency.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses a key distinction in Hanafi law: when an agency to sell is stipulated as a condition within a pledge contract, it acquires a binding force that ordinary agency lacks. The ruling protects the mortgagee's right by preventing the pledgor from unilaterally revoking the agent or terminating the agency upon death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Central Ruling
Read the first sentence: 'In the pledge contract, he is not discharged by his revocation, nor by the death of the pledgor and mortgagee.' State the ruling clearly.
The agent is not discharged by the pledgor's revocation or death, nor by the mortgagee's death.
2
Understand the Legal Reasoning (Illah)
The author explains that agency can be made conditional because it is a form of relinquishment (isqat). The pledgor, by authorizing the sale, has relinquished his right to prevent disposal. Relinquishments can be conditioned, making the agency binding once stipulated.
The illah is that the agency becomes a description of the pledge contract itself.
3
Compare with Separate Agency
Contrast this 'conditional agency' with a separate agency (wakalah mufradah). List the differences: the conditional agent can be compelled to sell, the agency survives death, etc.
Separate agency is revocable and terminates upon death of principal.
4
Analyze the Minor Case Dispute
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: if the pledgor ordered a minor to sell and the minor sells after reaching puberty. Abu Hanifa says the sale is invalid; the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is valid. Identify the basis of each view.
Abu Hanifa argues the order was void due to lack of capacity at the time; the Sahibayn focus on actual capacity at the time of sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في عقد الرهن لم ينعزل بعزله وبموت الراهن والمرتهن وتبطل بموت الوكيل حتى لا لا عند الامتثال هو لأن الوكالة يجوز تعليقها بالشرط لكونها من الإسقاطات لأن المانع من التصرف حق المالك، وبالتسليط على بيعه أسقط حقة، والإسقاطات يجوز تعليقها بالشروط . ولو أمر ببيعه صغيراً يعقل فباعه بعد ما بلغ لا يصح عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى. وقالا : يصح لقدرته عليه يقول إن أمره يقع باطلاً لعدم القدرة وقت الأمر فلا ينقلب جائزاً. قال رحمه الله : (فإن شرطت في عقد الرهن لم ينعزل بعزله وبموت الراهن والمرتهن لأن الوكالة لما شرطت في عقد الرهن صارت وصفاً من أوصافه وحقاً من حقوقة الا ترى أنها الزيادة الوثيقة فلزم بلزوم أصله ولا يتعلق به حق المرتهن وفي العزل إبطال حقه وصار كالوكالة بالخصومة بطلب المدعي، ولو وكله بالبيع مطلقاً حتى ملك البيع بالنقد والنسيئة ثم نهاه عن البيع بالنسيئة لم يعمل نهيه لأنه لازم بأصله فكذا ،بوصفه وكذا لا ينعزل بالعزل الحكمي لموت الموكل وارتداده ولحوقه بدار الحرب لأن الرهن لا يبطل بموته، ولو بطل إنما يبطل لحق الورثة وحق المرتهن مقدم عليه كما يقدم على حق الراهن بخلاف الوكالة المفردة حيث تبطل بالموت وينعزل بعزل الوكيل لما عرف في موضعه، وهذه الوكالة بخلاف المفردة من وجوه منها ما ذكرنا، ومنها أن الوكيل هنا إذا امتنع عن البيع يجبر عليه بخلاف الوكالة المفردة، ومنها أن هذا الولد والأرش بخلاف المفردة ومنها أنه إذا باع بخلاف جنس الدين له أن يبيع يصرفه إلى جنس الدين بخلاف المفردة ومنها أن الرهن إذا كان عبداً وقتله عبد فدفع القاتل بالجناية كان لهذا الوكيل أن يبيعه بخلاف المفردة، وإنما لم ينعزل بعزل المرتهن لأنه لم يوكله فكان أجنبياً عنه بالنسبة إلى الوكالة وهذا إذا عزله الموكل لا ينعزل فبعزل غيره أولى أن لا ينعزل .
In the pledge contract, he is not discharged by his revocation, nor by the death of the pledgor and mortgagee, and it becomes void by the death of the agent... because agency can be made conditional upon a stipulation since it is one of the [acts of] relinquishment because the preventer of disposal is the owner's right, and by authorizing him to sell he has relinquished his right, and relinquishments can be made conditional upon conditions. And if he ordered him to sell while he was a minor with understanding, and he sold it after reaching puberty, it is not valid according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. They two said: It is valid because he has the ability; he says that his order becomes void due to lack of ability at the time of the order, so it cannot become valid. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If it is stipulated in the pledge contract, he is not discharged by his revocation, nor by the death of the pledgor and mortgagee, because when the agency is stipulated in the pledge contract, it becomes a description of its descriptions and a right of its rights. Do you not see that it is the additional reinforcement, so it becomes binding with the binding of its origin, and the right of the mortgagee is not connected to it, and in revoking it is an annulment of his right, and it becomes like the agency for litigation at the request of the plaintiff. And if he authorized him absolutely to sell, so that he had the right to sell for cash and credit, then he forbade him from selling on credit, his prohibition does not take effect because it is binding in its origin, so likewise in its description. And similarly he is not discharged by the constructive revocation of the death of the principal, his apostasy, or his joining the abode of war, because the pledge does not become void by his death. And if it becomes void, it would be for the right of the heirs, and the right of the mortgagee takes precedence over it, just as it takes precedence over the right of the pledgor, contrary to the separate agency where it becomes void by death and he is discharged by the revocation of the agent as known in its place. And this agency is different from the separate one in several ways: from what we mentioned, and from that the agent here if he refrains from selling is compelled to do so, unlike the separate agency, and from that this [compensation for] offspring and [blood money?] is unlike the separate one, and from that if he sells for a different type of debt, he may sell and convert it to the type of debt, unlike the separate one, and from that if the pledge is a slave and he is killed by a slave, and the killer is handed over due to the crime, this agent can sell him, unlike the separate one. And he is not discharged by the revocation of the mortgagee because he did not authorize him, so he is a stranger to him with respect to the agency, and this is if the principal revokes him, he is not discharged, so by the revocation of someone else it is even more fitting that he not be discharged.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the status of the agent (wakil) appointed to sell the pledged item when the agency is a condition in the pledge contract itself. The author begins by stating the ruling: the agent is not discharged by the pledgor's revocation of the agency, nor by the death of the pledgor or the mortgagee. However, the agency does become void by the death of the agent himself. The reasoning is that since the agency is a condition in the pledge, it becomes an integral part of the contract. The pledgor, by authorizing the sale, has relinquished his right to prevent disposal, and such relinquishments can be conditioned. The author then contrasts this with a separate agency (wakalah mufradah), which is revoked by the principal's death and by the agent's discharge. Several differences are enumerated: the agent in a conditional agency can be compelled to sell, may sell the slave's offspring and blood money (if applicable), can convert sale proceeds to the type of debt, and can sell a substitute slave if the original is killed. The agent is not discharged by the mortgagee's revocation because the mortgagee did not appoint him. The overall principle is that the conditional agency is binding and inseparable from the pledge.

Key Terms
عقد الرهن (aqd al-rahn): The contract of pledge in which property is given as security for a debt.
الوكالة المفردة (al-wakalah al-mufradah): A separate agency independent of any other contract, which can be revoked at will and terminates upon the principal's death.
الإسقاطات (al-isqatat): Acts of relinquishment or dropping a right, which can be conditionalized in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the agency to sell is a condition in the pledge contract, what happens if the pledgor revokes the agency?
A) The agent is discharged immediately.
B) The agent is not discharged.
C) The pledge contract becomes void.
D) The mortgagee must appoint a new agent.

Key Takeaway
An agency conditioned in a pledge is binding and cannot be revoked unilaterally; it continues despite the death of the pledgor or mortgagee.

Agency After Pledge Contract: Separate or Attached?
Qualification that agency after pledge is separate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on an agency stipulated after a pledge contract, explain the reasoning of al-Karkhi and Abu Yusuf, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) regarding revocation and death of the pledgor.

Core Idea
Post-pledge agency is separate and revocable unless it was a condition in the original pledge.

Ibn Nujaym qualifies the earlier ruling that an agent appointed under a pledge is binding. That binding nature applies only if the agency was stipulated in the pledge contract itself. If the agency is appointed after the contract, a dispute arises: is it an independent, revocable agency or does it attach to the pledge and become binding? This lesson unpacks the two views within the Hanafi school and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger condition
Note that the author's phrase 'shartat fi aqd al-rahn' (if it is stipulated in the pledge contract) sets the boundary. The binding agency ruling applies only to that case. Our lesson concerns the other case: agency after the contract.
2
State al-Karkhi's position
Al-Karkhi holds that such an agency is 'wakalah mubtada'ah' (initial agency) — separate from the pledge. Thus the pledgor may dismiss the agent and the agency ends upon the pledgor's death.
This is the default Hanafi position on ordinary agency: revocable and terminates by death.
3
State Abu Yusuf's opposing view
A narration from Abu Yusuf and some later scholars holds that the post-pledge agency attaches to the contract (ilhaq bi al-aqd) and is binding, so the agent cannot be dismissed and is not discharged by the pledgor's death.
Some later Hanafi scholars chose this view.
4
Analyze the reasoning behind each view
Al-Karkhi: since the agency was not a condition of the pledge, it is independent. Abu Yusuf: the stipulation of sale is an increase (ziyadah) that enhances the fulfillment of the debt; increases in the subject matter of a contract attach to the original contract, making it as if it were originally stipulated.
The key analogy for Abu Yusuf is: like an increase in price after the sale, which is attached to the original sale.
5
Identify the practical difference (thamarah)
If the pledgor dies, under al-Karkhi the agent is automatically discharged, so the sale cannot proceed. Under Abu Yusuf, the agent remains authorized and can sell the pledged item to pay off the debt.
This affects the mortgagee's assurance of repayment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيد المؤلف بقوله : شرطت في عقد الرهن فلو كانت بعد عقد الرهن ذكر الكرخي في مختصره للراهن أن يعزله وينعزل بموته لأن التوكيل بالبيع وقع منفرداً عن الرهن. وإنما جعلناها من توابع الرهن لكونها مشروطة فيه، فإذا لم تشترط في الرهن اعتبرت وكالة مبتدأة، وروي عن أبي يوسف أنه لا ينعزل وهو اختيار بعض مشايخنا لأن المشروط بعد الرهن التحق بالعقد لأن اشتراط البيع حتى يوفي دينه من ثمنه زيادة إيفاء وتأكيد شرط في الرهن لأنه يثبت في الرهن إيفاء حكمي وباشتراط البيع فيه ثبت أيضاً حقيقي وكان اشتراط زيادة أيضاً، والزيادة في المعقود عليه تلتحق بأصل العقد وصار كالمشروط فيه ابتداء وكالزيادة في الثمن.
And the author restricted [the ruling] by his saying: 'if it is stipulated in the pledge contract'. So if it was after the pledge contract, al-Karkhi mentioned in his Mukhtasar that the pledgor may dismiss him and he is discharged by his death, because the authorization to sell occurred separately from the pledge. And we only made it one of the followers of the pledge because it is conditioned in it. So if it is not conditioned in the pledge, it is considered an initial agency. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he is not discharged, and this is the choice of some of our scholars, because that which is conditioned after the pledge is attached to the contract, because the stipulation of sale so that he may pay his debt from its price is an increase of fulfillment and an affirmation that is conditioned in the pledge, because in the pledge a constructive fulfillment is established, and by stipulating the sale in it, a real fulfillment is also established, and the stipulation is an increase, and the increase in the subject matter of the contract attaches to the original contract, and it becomes like that which is conditioned initially, and like the increase in the price.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage qualifies the previous ruling. The author, Ibn Nujaym, notes that the ruling about the agent not being discharged applies only when the agency is a condition in the pledge contract itself. If the agency is appointed after the pledge contract is concluded, it is a separate agency (wakalah mubtada'ah) and follows normal agency rules: the agent can be dismissed by the pledgor and is discharged by the pledgor's death. This is the view of al-Karkhi. However, a narration from Abu Yusuf states that even in this case the agent is not discharged, and some later scholars prefer this view. The reasoning is that the post-pledge stipulation attaches to the original contract because it enhances the fulfillment of the debt. The author mentions both views but does not strongly favor one; the student should note the difference between the two scenarios.

Key Terms
الوكالة المبتدأة (al-wakalah al-mubtada'ah): An agency that is initiated as a new independent contract, not as a condition of another contract.
التحق بالعقد (ilhaq bi al-aqd): Attachment of a subsequent condition to the original contract, making it part of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the practical difference (thamarah) between al-Karkhi's and Abu Yusuf's views on an agency appointed after a pledge contract?
A) The agent can never be dismissed.
B) The agency ends upon the pledgor's death under al-Karkhi but continues under Abu Yusuf.
C) The mortgagee must approve the agent under Abu Yusuf.
D) The agent becomes the owner of the pledged item under al-Karkhi.

Key Takeaway
An agency stipulated after a pledge contract is normally a separate revocable agency, but a minority Hanafi view attaches it to the pledge, making it binding.

Placing the Pawn with a Trustee: Judge's Authority and Disputes
Rulings on placing the pawn with a trustee, judge's role, and two narrations about the pledgor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on placing a pawn with a trustee, explain the judge's authority to place it with the mortgagee, and analyze the two intra-Hanafi narrations regarding placement with the pledgor.

Core Idea
The judge may place the pawn with the mortgagee despite the pledgor's objection, but placement with the pledgor is disputed.

In this lesson, we examine the rules governing where a pawn may be held after the contract. The passage clarifies the default permissibility of placing with the mortgagee, the judge's role when parties disagree, and a nuanced intra-Hanafi difference on placing the pawn with the pledgor himself. Understanding these details is crucial for correctly applying pledge law in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling and the parties' rights
The passage opens by stating that placing the pawn with the mortgagee is permissible because the right belongs to both parties. If they disagree, the judge appoints a trustee.
2
Examine the judge's authority to choose
The judge may also place the pawn with the mortgagee even if the pledgor refuses, and must avoid a trustee whom the mortgagee distrusts.
3
Analyze the two narrations on placement with the pledgor
One narration prohibits it (not beneficial), the other permits it (restriction from use still irritates). The text indicates preference for the first.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Understand the rationale behind each position
The purpose of pledge is to pressure the debtor to pay by withholding the pawn. If it is in his own hand, that pressure is lost; but the opposing view notes that he still cannot benefit from it.
5
Note the practical consequence of the dispute
Under the first narration, the judge should not place with the pledgor; under the second, he may. The relied-upon view is the first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرهن باب الرهن يوضع على يد عدل يدي فات من وهو متی آخر وقد مات الأول أو على يدي المرتهن جاز لأن الحق لهما، فإن اختلفا وضعه القاضي على عدل وإن شاء على يدي المرتهن لأنه ليس للراهن والمرتهن حق في الإمساك والحفظ فينصب القاضي عدلاً آخر يمسكه ويحفظه نائباً عنهما لأن القاضي نصب لإيفاء حقوق الناس، وإذا علم القاضي أن المرتهن يتهم العدل في العدالة لم يضعه على يديه وإن كره الراهن لأنه لما كان له ولاية الوضع على يدي عدل آخر مع إباء الراهن فكذا له ولاية الوضع على يدي المرتهن، فأما إذا أراد أن يضعه على يدي الراهن ذكر في بعض الروايات ليس له ذلك لأنه لا يفيد لأن المقصود من الرهن الاستيفاء وذلك بأن يضجر الراهن بإمساك الرهن عنه فيسارع في قضاء دينه وذلك لا يحصل متى كان الرهن في يده فيكون الوضع في يده اشتغالاً بما لا يفيد. وذكر في بعض الروايات له ذلك لأن الضجر لم يثبت من كل وجه لأن العين وإن كانت في يده لكن بقي ممنوعاً عن الانتفاع به فالحجر عن الانتفاع مما يضجره، وبإزاء ما الضجر حصل للمرتهن منفعة أخرى أنه هلك في يد الراهن لا يسقط من دينه كما لو أعاره منه وهلك في يده ولذا لو جعلاه على يد عدل أو سلطا رجلاً آخر على بيعه وسلم الثمن إلى المرتهن أو سلط المرتهن على بيعه جاز وليس له فسخه وعزله لما بينا. ولو عزلا العدل سلطا غيره أو لم يسلطا جاز لأنهما لو اتفقا على فسخ الرهن جاز فكذا على ما شرط فيه ومن التسليط على البيع المرتهن لو قبضه وجعل الراهن مسلطاً على بيعه جاز لأن الرهن أوجب حكمه وهو الحبس دائماً حين قبضه المرتهن فإذا فات القبض والحبس بعد ذلك فيتصور عوده في كل زمان لأن للمرتهن حق استرداده ولا يبطل عقد الرهن لأن فوات حكم العقد على وجه يتوهم ويرجى عوده لا يوجب بطلان العقد كما لو أعار من الراهن.
Book of Pledge, Chapter on the pledge placed on the hand of a trustee. ... on the hand of the mortgagee is permissible because the right belongs to both. If they disagree, the judge places it with a trustee, and if he wishes, on the hand of the mortgagee because neither the pledgor nor the mortgagee has a right to hold and preserve, so the judge appoints another trustee to hold and preserve as a deputy for both because the judge is appointed to fulfill people's rights. If the judge knows that the mortgagee accuses the trustee of lack of integrity, he does not place it on his hand even if the pledgor dislikes it because since he has authority to place it with another trustee despite the pledgor's refusal, so too he has authority to place it on the hand of the mortgagee. As for if he wants to place it on the hand of the pledgor, it is mentioned in some narrations that he does not have that because it is not beneficial, for the purpose of the pledge is collection (of debt) by irritating the pledgor through holding the pawn so he hastens to pay his debt, and that is not achieved when the pawn is in his hand, so placing it in his hand is an occupation with no benefit. And it is mentioned in some narrations that he has that because irritation is not established from every aspect; even though the item is in his hand, he remains prevented from benefiting from it, so restriction from benefit irritates him, and in exchange for the irritation the mortgagee gets another benefit: if it perishes in the pledgor's hand, nothing of his debt is dropped, just as if he lent it to him and it perished in his hand. For this reason, if they both place it with a trustee or authorize another man to sell it and deliver the price to the mortgagee, or authorize the mortgagee to sell it, it is permissible, and he does not have the right to revoke or dismiss him, as we explained. And if they both dismiss the trustee and authorize another or do not authorize, it is permissible because if they agree to cancel the pledge, it is permissible, so too regarding what is stipulated therein. And regarding authorizing the mortgagee to sell, if he takes possession and makes the pledgor authorized to sell it, it is permissible because the pledge necessitates its ruling, which is detention, permanently when the mortgagee takes possession; if possession and detention are lost thereafter, its return is conceivable at all times because the mortgagee has the right to reclaim it, and the contract of pledge is not invalidated because loss of the contract's ruling in a way that its return is hoped for does not necessitate invalidity, just as if he lent it to the pledgor.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It begins by stating the basic ruling: the pledge may be placed with the mortgagee because both parties have an interest. If they disagree, the judge appoints a trustee. The judge may also place it with the mortgagee even if the pledgor objects, since the pledgor has no right to insist on a specific trustee. However, if the judge knows the mortgagee will not trust the trustee, he avoids that. Two narrations are mentioned about placing the pawn with the pledgor himself: one says it is not allowed because it does not achieve the purpose of irritating the pledgor to pay; the other says it is allowed because even in the pledgor's hand, he cannot use it, which still irritates him, and the mortgagee gains security. The passage then discusses cases where both parties agree to authorize a sale, and the permissibility of such arrangements. It also notes that if the mortgagee takes possession and then authorizes the pledgor to sell, the pledge contract remains valid because the detention can be re-established.

Key Terms
العدل (al-adl): The trustee who holds the pawn on behalf of both parties
المرتهن (al-murtahin): The mortgagee (creditor) who receives the pawn
الراهن (al-rahin): The pledgor (debtor) who gives the pawn

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the judge knows the mortgagee accuses the trustee of dishonesty, where should the judge place the pawn?
A) With the trustee despite the accusation
B) With the mortgagee
C) With the pledgor
D) With a different trustee

Key Takeaway
The judge may place the pawn with the mortgagee even if the pledgor objects, but placing it with the pledgor is not the preferred view.

Condition That Trustee Is the Pledgor Invalidates the Pledge
Ruling with talil using qiyas, then subsidiary rulings on agency and substitution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the pledgor is stipulated as trustee in a pledge contract and explain the reasoning (talil) using qiyas.

Core Idea
Stipulating the pledgor as trustee in a pledge contract invalidates the pledge, even if possession occurs.

This lesson examines a critical condition in the pledge (rahn) contract according to the Hanafi school. The essence of a valid pledge requires that the pawn be held by the mortgagee or a neutral trustee. If the parties stipulate at the time of the contract that the pledgor himself acts as trustee, the contract becomes invalid (fasid) regardless of whether the mortgagee later takes possession. The reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy) to a similar invalid conditional statement. The passage also explores related scenarios of agency and substitution of the pawn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Stipulated Condition
Find the specific condition mentioned in the contract: that the trustee (adl) be the pledgor himself. This is a condition contrary to the nature of a pledge.
The condition is explicit in the contract's formation, not added later.
2
Determine the Ruling on Validity
The text states that if this condition is stipulated within the pledge contract, the pledge is not valid (la yasihh al-rahn) even if the mortgagee (murtahin) takes physical possession of the pawn.
Possession cannot cure a condition that contradicts the essence of the contract.
3
Analyze the Reasoning (Talil) via Qiyas
The author provides an analogy: just as saying 'I will not pledge a house for a day and a day' is invalid because it negates the purpose of pledge, so is stipulating the pledgor as trustee invalid because the purpose of pledge is to secure the debt by detaining the pawn with the mortgagee.
The analogy highlights that the condition nullifies the core function of rahn.
4
Examine the Authorization Scenario
If the pledgor authorizes a person to sell the pawn without the mortgagee taking possession, it is not a pledge (due to lack of possession). That person is merely an agent (wakil), not a trustee in the pledge sense.
The distinction between pledge and agency is crucial for rights of creditors.
5
Apply to Substitution Cases
When the pawn is substituted (e.g., a slave replaces a damaged one), the authorized person's authority extends to the substitute because the mortgagee's right attached to the original. This differs from a pure agent who has no such extension.
This shows the difference in authority between a pledge-related trustee and a mere agent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا إذا شرطا بعد الرهن فأما إذا شرطا في الرهن أن يكون العدل هو الراهن لا يصح الرهن وإن قبضه المرتهن لأنه شرط في الرهن أن يكون الرهن عنده ساعة فلا يجوز كما لو قال يوماً ويوماً لا ارتهن داراً وسلط الراهن رجلاً على بيعها وإيفاء الثمن ولم يقبضها المرتهن لم يكن رهناً لعدم قبضه بنفسه ولا بنائبه وبيع العدل إياها جائز بالوكالة والثمن يدفع إلى الراهن، فإن دفعه إلى المرتهن لم يضمن وينعزل العدل بموت الراهن والرهن أسوة الغرماء لأن الرهن لم يصح فلم يتعلق حق المرتهن بالثمن إلا أنه أمره بالبيع وبقضاء الدين من الثمن والمأمور بقضاء الدين إن شاء دفع إلى الآمر، وإن شاء دفع إلى الغريم، ويكون هذا وكيلاً لا يجبر العبد على البيع وينعزل بموت الآمر لأنه شرط البيع في رهن غير لازم فلا يكون البيع لازماً ولو قتل العبد المرهون عبد العدل المسلط على بيعه أو فقأ عينه عبد فدفع مكانه فهو مسلط على بيعه بمنزلة الأول لأن العبد المدفوع صار رهناً لأن حق المرتهن كان ثابتاً في الأول والبدل قائم مقام الأول فثبتت ولايته في الثاني حسب ثبوت ولايته في الأول بخلاف الوكيل المفرد لأنه ما ثبت له حق بيع الأصل حتى يسري إلى بدله.
And this applies if they stipulate after the pledge. But if they stipulate in the pledge that the trustee be the pledgor, the pledge is not valid even if the mortgagee takes possession because it is a condition in the pledge that the pawn be with him at the time, so it is not permissible, just as if he said 'a day and a day' I do not pledge a house. And if the pledgor authorizes a man to sell it and pay the price and the mortgagee did not take possession, it is not a pledge due to lack of possession by himself or his agent. The sale by the trustee is permissible by agency, and the price is paid to the pledgor. If he pays it to the mortgagee, he is not liable, and the trustee is dismissed by the death of the pledgor, and the pledge is like other creditors because the pledge was not valid, so the mortgagee's right did not attach to the price. However, he ordered him to sell and pay the debt from the price, and the one ordered to pay the debt may pay to the orderer or to the creditor. This person is an agent; the slave is not forced to sell, and he is dismissed by the death of the principal because the sale was stipulated in a non-binding pledge, so the sale is not binding. And if the pledged slave kills the slave of the trustee authorized to sell, or gouges his eye, and he gives another slave in exchange, that slave is authorized to sell like the first because the exchanged slave becomes a pawn since the mortgagee's right was established in the first, and the substitute stands in its place, so his authority is established in the second just as it was established in the first, unlike a mere agent because he did not have the right to sell the original so as to extend to its substitute.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about conditions in the pledge contract. It distinguishes between stipulations made after the contract (which are valid) and stipulations made within the contract itself (which may invalidate it). If the parties stipulate at the time of the contract that the trustee (adl) should be the pledgor himself, the pledge is invalid even if the mortgagee takes possession. The reason is that the essence of a pledge requires the pawn to be in the possession of the mortgagee or his trustee, not the pledgor. An analogy is given: if someone says 'I do not pledge a house for a day and a day,' it is invalid. Then the text discusses a scenario where the pledgor authorizes a person to sell the pawn without the mortgagee taking possession; this is not a valid pledge because the mortgagee never possessed it. That person is merely an agent. The text also covers the effect of the pledgor's death on such an agency, and the case of substitution of the pawn (e.g., if the pledged slave is exchanged for another). The authority of the trustee extends to the substitute because the mortgagee's right was attached to the original, but this is unlike a mere agent who does not have such authority over substitutes.

Key Terms
العدل (al-adl): Trustee who holds the pawn; here the stipulation that the pledgor be the trustee is invalid
شرط (shart): Condition; a stipulation in the contract that may affect validity
قبض (qabd): Possession; taking delivery of the pawn

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if the parties stipulate in the pledge contract that the trustee be the pledgor, and the mortgagee later takes possession?
A) The pledge becomes valid upon possession.
B) The pledge is invalid even with possession.
C) The pledge is valid but the condition is void.
D) The pledge is suspended until a neutral trustee is appointed.

Key Takeaway
A condition in a pledge contract that the pledgor be the trustee invalidates the pledge (fasid) regardless of later possession, because it contradicts the essence of pledge which requires detention of the pawn with the mortgagee or a neutral party.

Trustee Qualifications and Effect of Death
Ruling on trustee qualifications and death of agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who may serve as a trustee and explain why the trustee's authority terminates upon death, distinguishing it from mudaraba.

Core Idea
Agency dies with the agent; it is not inherited, unlike mudaraba which passes to heirs.

In this passage, the author clarifies who can act as a trustee for a pawn and the critical difference between agency and mudaraba regarding death. The trustee's authority is personal and ends at death; heirs do not inherit the role. This contrasts with mudaraba, where the partnership right is inherited. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rulings on pawn transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify permissible trustees
List the types of persons who can be trustees: restricted/unrestricted slave, intelligent child (authorized or not). Note that they are not liable unless authorized by master/guardian.
The liability (dhimmah) is limited because slaves and children cannot guarantee statements without permission.
2
Analyze the effect of the agent's death
The text states that agency terminates upon death; neither heir nor executor stands in the agent's place. The reason is that agency is a right upon the agent (haqq 'alayhi), not a right for him (haqq lahu).
Compare with mudaraba where it is a right for the mudarib and thus inherited.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's dissenting view
Abu Yusuf holds that if the agent makes a will, the executor may sell by analogy to mudaraba. The author rebuts by distinguishing the nature of the right.
This intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is resolved by the majority holding that agency is personal.
4
Understand the ruling on bequeathing sale
A bequest to sell the pawn is invalid unless it was already stipulated in the agency contract, because the agency is binding by placement.
The key is whether the agency was originally established as binding (lazim).
5
Conclude with the trustee's death
The passage concludes with a quote from al-Dhakhira: if the trustee dies, the authorization is void.
This reinforces the general principle that agency is personal and non-transferable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كان العدل عبداً محجوراً أو غير محجوراً أو صبياً عاقلاً مأذوناً وغير مأذون جاز ، ولا تلزمهما العهدة إلا بإذن المولى والولي لأنهما لا يؤاخذان بضمان الأقوال إلا بإذن المولى والولي. قال : وتبطل بموت الوكيل حتى لا يقوم وارثه ولا وصيه مقامه لأن الوكالة رحمه لا يجري فيها الإرث ولأن الموكل رضي برأيه لا برأي غيره. وعن أبي يوسف أنه إن وصى الوكيل يملك بيعه لأن الوكالة لازمة فيملك الوصي كالمضارب إذا مات والمالية عروض المضارب بيعها لما أنه لازم بعد ما صار عروضاً . قلنا : الوكالة حق على الوكيل فلا تورث عنه لأن الإرث يجري في حق له لا في حق عليه فوجب القول ببطلانها لا بخلاف المضاربة لأنها حق المضارب فيورث عنه فتقوم الورثة مقامه فيه، ولأن المضارب له ولاية التوكيل في حياته فجاز أن يقوم وصيه مقامه بعد وفاته كالأب في مال الصغير والوكيل ليس له حق التوكيل في حياته فلا يقوم غيره مقامه بعد موته. ولو أوصى لرجل بيعه لم يصح إلا إذا كان مشروطاً له في الوكالة فيصح لأنه لازم بوضعه. وفي الذخيرة: لو مات العدل بطل التسليط . وفي السراجية : العدل المسلط على البيع إذا باع البعض بطل الرهن في الباقي، وإذا باع العدل الرهن ووقع الاختلاف بين الراهن والمرتهن والعدل في مقدار الثمن فقال العدل بعت بمائة فأعطيتها المرتهن وقال المرتهن باعه بخمسين فالقول للمرتهن مع يمينه ؛ كذا في الخانية، وإن أقام البينة فالبينة بينة الراهن، وإذا كان العدل مسلطاً على البيع إذا حل الأجل فقال المرتهن كان الأجل إلى شهر رمضان وقد دخل شهر رمضان وقال الراهن إلى شوال فالقول قول الراهن في وقت حلول الأجل القول قول المرتهن وإذا باع العدل بالنسيئة جاز البيع من غير تفصيل؛ كذا في الأصل. وفي غيره : إذا باع بنسيئة غير معهودة بأن باع إلى عشر سنين ينبغي أن لا تجوز عندهما. وقال القاضي أبو علي النسفي : إن تقدم من الراهن ما يدل على البيع بالنقد بأن قال المرتهن يطالبني بدينه ويؤذيني فبعه حتى أوفيه فباعه بالنسيئة لا يجوز بمنزلة ما لو قال بعه فإني محتاج إلى النفقة وفي الذخيرة: لو كان المرتهن هو فقال له الراهن بعه واستوف دينك من ثمنه فباعه بالنسيئة يجوز كيفما كان. وقال شمس الأئمة السرخسي : لو لحق العدل جنون يقع الإياس من إفاقته فينعزل، وإن كان يرجى إفاقته لا ينعزل حتى إذا عاد عقله إليه له أن يبيع وإن باع في حال جنونه والعدل في يصح، حق العين كالمودع فما جاز للمودع جاز للعدل ولا يملك أن يسافر بالرهن إذا كانت الطريق مخيفة، وإذا كان الطريق آمناً وقيد بالمصر لا يملك السفر، وفي الغياثية : إذا مات المرتهن يبيع العدل العين المرهونة بحضرة الورثة ولو باع العدل ثم رد عليه بعيب رجع به على الراهن إلا أن يكون الرد عليه بإقراره بعيب جاز إن يحدث في المدة ولو صدقه الراهن بالعيب في يده يرجع به عليه، ولو اختار العدل أحدهما فأفلس ليس له أن يرجع على الآخر. ولو قال العدل
And if the trustee is a restricted slave or unrestricted, or an intelligent child, authorized or unauthorized, it is permissible, and they are not liable unless with permission of the master or guardian because they are not held for warranty of statements except with permission of the master or guardian. He said: And the agency becomes void with the death of the agent, so that neither his heir nor his executor stands in his place because agency is a mercy and inheritance does not apply to it, and because the principal was satisfied with his opinion, not the opinion of another. And from Abu Yusuf that if the agent makes a will, he may sell it because the agency is binding, so the executor may sell, like a mudarib when he dies and the capital is merchandise, the mudarib's capital is sold because it is binding after it becomes merchandise. We said: Agency is a right upon the agent, so it is not inherited from him because inheritance applies to rights for him, not rights upon him, so it must be said that it becomes void, unlike mudaraba because it is a right for the mudarib, so it is inherited from him, and his heirs stand in his place, and because the mudarib has the authority to delegate during his life, so it is permissible for his executor to stand in his place after his death, like the father regarding the minor's property, but the agent does not have the right to delegate during his life, so no one else stands in his place after his death. And if he bequeaths to a man to sell it, it is not valid unless it was stipulated in the agency, then it is valid because it is binding by its placement. In al-Dhakhira: If the trustee dies, the authorization is void. In al-Sirajiyya: The trustee authorized to sell, if he sells some, the pledge becomes void for the rest. And if the trustee sells the pawn and there is a dispute between the pledgor, mortgagee, and trustee about the amount of the price—the trustee says 'I sold for one hundred and gave it to the mortgagee,' and the mortgagee says 'He sold it for fifty'—the word is the mortgagee's with his oath; thus in al-Khaniyya. And if he produces evidence, the evidence is the evidence of the pledgor. And if the trustee is authorized to sell when the term arrives, and the mortgagee says 'the term was until Ramadan and Ramadan has entered,' and the pledgor says 'until Shawwal,' the word is the pledgor's regarding the time of the term's arrival, and the word is the mortgagee's regarding sale. And if the trustee sells on credit, the sale is permissible without details; thus in al-Asl. In other [books]: if he sells on an unusual credit, e.g., for ten years, it should not be permissible according to them. And Qadi Abu Ali al-Nasafi said: If the pledgor indicated sale for cash by saying 'the mortgagee is demanding his debt and troubling me, so sell it until I pay him,' and he sold it on credit, it is not permissible, just as if he said 'sell it, for I need maintenance.' In al-Dhakhira: If the mortgagee is the one, and the pledgor says to him 'sell it and take your debt from its price,' and he sold it on credit, it is permissible however it was. And Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: If the trustee becomes insane with no hope of recovery, he is dismissed; if recovery is hoped for, he is not dismissed, until his reason returns, then he may sell; if he sells during his insanity, the trustee is not valid? The right concerning the item is like a deposit, so what is permissible for the depositor is permissible for the trustee; and he is not allowed to travel with the pawn if the road is dangerous; if the road is safe and it is restricted to the city, he is not allowed to travel. In al-Ghiyathiyya: If the mortgagee dies, the trustee sells the pawned item in the presence of the heirs. And if the trustee sells and then it is returned to him due to a defect, he recovers from the pledgor, unless the return is due to his acknowledgment of a defect that occurred during the period; and if the pledgor confirms the defect was in his hand, he recovers from him. And if the trustee chooses one of them and he becomes insolvent, he does not have the right to recourse against the other. And if the trustee says...
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof covering many details about the trustee's authority to sell the pawn. It begins by stating who can be a trustee: a slave (restricted or not) or an intelligent child (authorized or not) are acceptable, but they are not liable for warranty unless authorized by their master/guardian. Then it discusses the effect of the agent's death: the agency terminates and is not inherited, unlike mudaraba (partnership) which passes to heirs. This is because agency is a right upon the agent, not a right for him. A bequest to sell is invalid unless the agency was already binding. The passage then cites various authoritative works: al-Dhakhira states that the trustee's authorization is void upon his death; al-Sirajiyya states that if the trustee sells only part, the pledge becomes void for the remainder; disputes about the sale price are resolved by the mortgagee's word (with oath), but if evidence is brought, the pledgor's evidence is preferred. Disputes about the term: the pledgor's word regarding when it ends, the mortgagee's regarding the right to sell. The trustee may sell on credit without restriction according to al-Asl, but unusual credit (e.g., ten years) is not permissible. If the pledgor indicated cash sale, selling on credit is invalid. If the mortgagee himself is authorized, any credit is fine. The insanity of the trustee: if hopeless, he is dismissed; if recovery is expected, he remains. He cannot travel with the pawn if the road is dangerous or if restricted to the city. After the mortgagee's death, the trustee sells in the presence of heirs. If the sold item is returned due to a defect, the trustee recovers from the pledgor unless the defect was acknowledged by the trustee. If the trustee chooses one of two (debtors?) and that one becomes insolvent, he cannot recourse against the other.

Key Terms
العدل (al-adl): Trustee authorized to sell the pawn; has rights similar to a depositary
الوكالة (al-wikalah): Agency; distinguished from the trustee's role because agency ends at death and is not inherited

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is agency not inherited, unlike mudaraba?
A) Because agency is a right for the agent (haqq lahu).
B) Because agency is a right upon the agent (haqq alayhi).
C) Because agency can be terminated at any time.
D) Because agency does not involve property.

Key Takeaway
Agency is personal and non-inheritable; upon death, authorization to sell a pawn is void.

Disputes on Price, Term, and Credit Sale
Rulings on disputes and credit sales.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for resolving disputes between pledgor, mortgagee, and trustee regarding sale price and term, and determine the validity of credit sales.

Core Idea
In price disputes, the mortgagee's word prevails with oath; in term disputes, the pledgor's word on term ending and mortgagee's on right to sell.

This passage provides practical guidance for when the trustee sells the pawn and disputes arise among the parties. It covers three key areas: disagreement over the sale price, disagreement over when the sale could take place, and the validity of selling on credit. Understanding who bears the burden of proof and what terms are permissible is crucial for trustees and parties to avoid invalid sales.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the price dispute scenario
The trustee says he sold for 100 and gave the money to the mortgagee; the mortgagee says the trustee sold for 50. The ruling: the mortgagee's word is taken with his oath. If evidence is presented, the pledgor's evidence is preferred.
This is the default rule; the mortgagee is deemed the rightful claimant regarding the price.
2
Understand the term dispute scenario
The mortgagee says the term was until Ramadan (now entered), the pledgor says until Shawwal. For the question of when the term ends, the pledgor's word prevails; for the question of whether the trustee has the right to sell now, the mortgagee's word prevails.
This dichotomy reflects different aspects: the term itself (pledgor's benefit) vs. the right to sell (mortgagee's benefit).
3
Examine the ruling on credit sale
The base ruling (al-Asl) states that the trustee may sell on credit without restriction. However, other authorities restrict that if the credit is unusual (e.g., 10 years), it is not permissible (according to them).
The general permissibility is from Zahir al-Riwayah, but later scholars qualify it.
4
Consider the pledgor's indication for cash sale
Qadi al-Nasafi rules: if the pledgor indicated a cash sale (e.g., said 'sell it to pay off my debt'), then selling on credit is invalid. This is analogous to saying 'sell it because I need maintenance'.
The indication restricts the trustee's authority.
5
Review the exception for mortgagee as seller
If the mortgagee himself is authorized by the pledgor to sell, then selling on credit is permissible regardless of the term, because he acts as the pledgor's agent and the pledgor's own right is involved.
This is from al-Dhakhira.

الوكيل حتى لا يقوم وارثه ولا وصيه مقامه لأن الوكالة رحمه لا يجري فيها الإرث ولأن الموكل رضي برأيه لا برأي غيره. وعن أبي يوسف أنه إن وصى الوكيل يملك بيعه لأن الوكالة لازمة فيملك الوصي كالمضارب إذا مات والمالية عروض المضارب بيعها لما أنه لازم بعد ما صار عروضاً . قلنا : الوكالة حق على الوكيل فلا تورث عنه لأن الإرث يجري في حق له لا في حق عليه فوجب القول ببطلانها لا بخلاف المضاربة لأنها حق المضارب فيورث عنه فتقوم الورثة مقامه فيه، ولأن المضارب له ولاية التوكيل في حياته فجاز أن يقوم وصيه مقامه بعد وفاته كالأب في مال الصغير والوكيل ليس له حق التوكيل في حياته فلا يقوم غيره مقامه بعد موته. ولو أوصى لرجل بيعه لم يصح إلا إذا كان مشروطاً له في الوكالة فيصح لأنه لازم بوضعه. وفي الذخيرة: لو مات العدل بطل التسليط . وفي السراجية : العدل المسلط على البيع إذا باع البعض بطل الرهن في الباقي، وإذا باع العدل الرهن ووقع الاختلاف بين الراهن والمرتهن والعدل في مقدار الثمن فقال العدل بعت بمائة فأعطيتها المرتهن وقال المرتهن باعه بخمسين فالقول للمرتهن مع يمينه ؛ كذا في الخانية، وإن أقام البينة فالبينة بينة الراهن، وإذا كان العدل مسلطاً على البيع إذا حل الأجل فقال المرتهن كان الأجل إلى شهر رمضان وقد دخل شهر رمضان وقال الراهن إلى شوال فالقول قول الراهن في وقت حلول الأجل القول قول المرتهن وإذا باع العدل بالنسيئة جاز البيع من غير تفصيل؛ كذا في الأصل. وفي غيره : إذا باع بنسيئة غير معهودة بأن باع إلى عشر سنين ينبغي أن لا تجوز عندهما. وقال القاضي أبو علي النسفي : إن تقدم من الراهن ما يدل على البيع بالنقد بأن قال المرتهن يطالبني بدينه ويؤذيني فبعه حتى أوفيه فباعه بالنسيئة لا يجوز بمنزلة ما لو قال بعه فإني محتاج إلى النفقة وفي الذخيرة: لو كان المرتهن هو فقال له الراهن بعه واستوف دينك من ثمنه فباعه بالنسيئة يجوز كيفما كان. وقال شمس الأئمة السرخسي : لو لحق العدل جنون يقع الإياس من إفاقته فينعزل، وإن كان يرجى إفاقته لا ينعزل حتى إذا عاد عقله إليه له أن يبيع وإن باع في حال جنونه والعدل في يصح، حق العين كالمودع فما جاز للمودع جاز للعدل ولا يملك أن يسافر بالرهن إذا كانت الطريق مخيفة، وإذا كان الطريق آمناً وقيد بالمصر لا يملك السفر، وفي الغياثية : إذا مات المرتهن يبيع العدل العين المرهونة بحضرة الورثة ولو باع العدل ثم رد عليه بعيب رجع به على الراهن إلا أن يكون الرد عليه بإقراره بعيب جاز إن يحدث في المدة ولو صدقه الراهن بالعيب في يده يرجع به عليه، ولو اختار العدل أحدهما فأفلس ليس له أن يرجع
