Kharaj and Ushr Payment Effect on Pledge
Clarifies that paying land tax does not affect the pledged property or reduce the debt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the effect of land tax (kharaj/ushr) payments on a pledged property and identify the exception when the tax is taken unjustly.

Core Idea
Paying land tax does not reduce debt or affect pledge; only unjust seizure by the ruler does.

When a debtor owns land encumbered with tax and has pledged property to secure a loan, paying the tax might seem to affect the debt. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that such payment generally does not impact the pledge. However, there is a critical exception when the tax is taken unjustly, which we will explore.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage discusses three situations: (1) tax taken from the debtor personally, (2) tax taken from the produce of the land, and (3) tax taken unjustly by the ruler. Identify which scenario is being discussed.
2
Apply the general rule
For the first two scenarios, the ruling is that the tax payment does not reduce the debt or affect the pledge. Understand the reasoning: the tax is an independent obligation; the produce is a separate increase.
3
Recognize the exception
For the third scenario, when the ruler takes the tax unjustly, it is treated as usurpation (ghasb) and proportionally reduces the debt. Note the parallel to destruction of part of the pledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كان للراهن أرض خراج أو عشر وأخذ الخراج والعشر من الراهن لا يرجع في ثمنه لأن الراهن صار قاضياً حقاً واجباً عليه فلا يرجع به في حال تعلق به حق غيره، وإن أخذ ذلك من الثمرة أو الغلة لا يبطل شيئاً من الرهن لأن هلاك الزيادة من العين لا يسقط شيئاً من الثمن ويكون ذلك محسوباً على الراهن، ولأنه لو لم يستحق شيئاً من العين فإن لصاحب الأرض أن يعطي الخراج من مال آخر فلم يصر شيء من الدين مستحقاً إلا إذا أخذه السلطان بغير حق فإنه يسقط من الدين بقدره لأنه غصب منه فصار كما لو هلك بعض الرهن في يده.
If the debtor has land subject to kharaj or ushr, and the kharaj or ushr is taken from the debtor, he does not revert to its price, because the debtor has become a payer of a right obligatory upon him, so he does not revert to it while a right of another is attached to it. And if it (the tax) is taken from the fruit or produce, it does not invalidate anything of the pledge, because the destruction of an increase from the property does not reduce any of the price, and that is counted against the debtor. And because even if he did not deserve anything of the property, the owner of the land could give the kharaj from other wealth, so nothing of the debt becomes due except if the ruler takes it unjustly; then it reduces the debt proportionally, because it is usurpation from him, so it is as if part of the pledge perished in his hand.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the interaction between land tax (kharaj/ushr) and a pledge. The scenario: the debtor owns land that is encumbered with tax; he borrows money and pledges some property. The tax is collected from the debtor personally (not from the pledged property). The ruling: the debtor cannot recoup the tax payment from the proceeds of the pledged property (the price when sold). The reason is that the tax is an independent obligation of the debtor, and once paid, it is a discharge of a duty; it does not create a claim against the pledged property which is already subject to the creditor's right. If the tax is taken from the produce (fruit or yield) of the pledged land itself (assuming the land is not the pledge but the produce may be part of the estate), that does not reduce the pledge because the produce is a separate increase (ziyadah); its loss does not affect the original pledged item. The tax payment is considered an expense on the debtor. However, if the ruler (sultan) takes the tax unjustly (i.e., more than due or without right), then that unjustly taken amount reduces the debt proportionally, as it is treated as usurpation (ghasb) from the debtor, akin to the pledged property being partially destroyed.

Key Terms
الخراج (al-kharāj): Land tax imposed on agricultural land owned by non-Muslims or subject to tribute.
العشر (al-‘ushr): Tithe (10% tax) on agricultural land of Muslims.
الزيادة (al-ziyādah): Increase or produce from the pledged property (e.g., fruits, offspring).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the ruler takes kharaj unjustly from the debtor, what is the effect on the debt secured by the pledge?
A) The debt is reduced proportionally.
B) The debt is unaffected.
C) The pledge is released.
D) The debtor may sue the ruler.

Key Takeaway
Payment of land tax (kharaj/ushr) does not affect a pledge; only unjust seizure by the ruler proportionally reduces the debt.
